Life of the Author
intermediate

Ash'ari Scholars and Rational Sciences: Defense of Engagement
Author defends Ash'ari engagement with philosophy, citing al-Razi and al-Amidi as examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the main arguments Bahr al-'Ulum uses to justify Ash'ari scholars' study of philosophy and explain how he distinguishes their method from Peripatetic philosophy.

Core Idea
Studying philosophy was a religious duty for Ash'ari imams, not a compromise of their creed.

In this passage from his commentary on Sullam al-'Ulum, Bahr al-'Ulum responds to critics who accuse Ash'ari scholars of abandoning their creed by engaging with philosophy. He constructs a historical and methodological defense, citing examples of leading imams who studied rational sciences while remaining steadfast in their Ash'ari identity. Understanding this argument is crucial for appreciating how Islamic scholars navigated the relationship between revealed and rational knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's central thesis
Read the opening lines: Bahr al-'Ulum asserts that studying rational sciences was a religious obligation ('mimmā awjabahu Allāh). This frames the entire passage as a defense, not a mere justification.
The author sets the tone by invoking divine obligation, elevating the issue beyond personal choice.
2
Examine the historical evidence
Look at the examples given: al-Taj al-Subki's praise of al-Ghazali and al-Razi, Ibn 'Abd al-Salam's defense of al-Amidi. Each example shows that prominent Ash'ari authorities approved of engagement with philosophy while remaining vigilant guardians of creed.
The author uses a 'witness' strategy: citing respected figures to lend credibility.
3
Analyze the distinction between Ash'ari theology and Peripatetic philosophy
The author explicitly states that 'Ash'ari discourse was never an ally of Peripatetic philosophy' and quotes al-Razi's criticism of Ibn Sina's 'Uyun al-Hikmah. This shows the method is critical engagement, not adoption.
Al-Razi's hesitation and opposition are used to argue that Ash'ari scholars approach philosophy with a critical eye.
4
Evaluate the conclusion on loyalty to creed
The author concludes that the imams 'did not abandon Ash'arism and did not accuse it of backwardness.' He attributes this to divine success, fulfillment of conditions (like those of al-Subki), and pure intentions for serving Islam.
The conclusion reinforces that philosophical study is compatible with orthodox faith when conducted with proper intent and methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرح بحر العلوم على سلم العلوم

الإسلام والعلوم العقلية

ولا شك أن هذا الذي فعله هؤلاء الأئمة هو مما أوجبه الله تعالى عليهم ؛ للدفاع عن حرم الإسلام ،وقدسيته وتثبيت قلوب المؤمنين به، فلا يُلامون أبدا، بل جهودهم مشكورة سرمدا. وهذا التاج السبكي، رأينا كيف كان يكره الفلسفة اليونانية والمشائية، ولكن وجدناه يثني على الغزالي والرازي، وكذلك يثني على البيضاوي والآمدي وغيرهم ممن تسربل بعلوم هؤلاء الفلاسفة، وخاض فيها، وأثنى عليهم، وهو الحارس المتيقظ لعقائد المسلمين، لا يترك صغيرة ولا كبيرة تمس كرامتها وصفائها إلا أحصاها، لم يطعن في هؤلاء الأئمة قط.

وقد اشتهر صيت سلطان العلماء عز الدين بن عبد السلام كفقيه على سمت السلف، ومحدث متحفظ، ولا يختلف اثنان في إمامته وجلالة قدره، وقد سُئِل عن شيخه سيف الدين الآمدي الذي كثرت وقيعة المجسمة فيه؛ لأسباب، منها اشتغاله بهذه العلوم، فماذا كان رده على السؤال؟ قال: إن خرج زنديق لهدم الإسلام تعين الآمدي للرد عليه في هذا الزمان، وهو الذي خرج في جنازته حين توفي الآمدي، فخرج معه خلق لا يحصى.

ومما يجب التنبيه هنا أن أئمتنا الأشاعرة رضوان الله عليهم أجمعين لم يتخلوا عن الأشعرية ولم يتهموها بالتخلف بعد أن خاضوا في تلك العلوم المليئة بسموم الشبهات والخيالات المريبات، حتى صاروا أئمة يشار إليهم بالبنان في تلك الفنون، وصار من السهل لهم جدا أن يفتخروا على إخوانهم الأشاعرة، أو يتكبروا عليهم، إلى درجة أن يخرجوا على المذهب ويطعنوا فيه وفي تراثه وأئمته، إلا أن شيئا من ذلك لم يحدث، بل بقي كل منهم على تمسكه الذي كان عليه قبل الدخول في هذه العلوم، ليس في الأصول فقط، بل حتى في الفروع، وهكذا الرازي أشعري شافعي حتى النخاع، والآمدي أشعري شافعي في دمه ولحمه. وذلك أولا بتوفيق من الله، وثانيا: لتوفر الشروط التي أشار إليها التاج السبكي فيهم، وثالثا لحسن نواياهم وطيب مقاصدهم، هي خدمة دين الإسلام، فحق على الله - بسابق وعده - أن يهدي كل من جاهد فيه سبله.

ولم يكن الكلام الأشعري حليفا للفلسفة المشائية أبدا، ولا اتخذ منهجنا الكلامي منها رفيقا أو صديقا في أي فترة من فترات التاريخ، ولم يكن متكلمو أهل السنة ملتزمين قط بالإيمان بكل ما بين دفتي «الشفاء» و«الإشارات»، بل الحرب قائمة بين المنهجين منذ البداية وإلى الآن. انظر إلى أروع ما يقوله المتكلم السني الأشعري على لسان الإمام الرازي، فخر الملة والدين، وهو يتصدى لشرح عيون الحكمة لابن سينا يبين أنه لماذا أحجم عن شرحه إلى الآن، قائلا: «أحجمت عنه لأمور .... ثانيها: أني مخالف لمقتضى هذا الكتاب في دقيقه وجليله، وجمله وتفاصيله، فإن جررت عليها ذيل المهادنة والمداهنة صِرتُ كالراضي بتوجيه العباد إلى مسالك الغي والفساد، وإن تشمرت للكشف والبيان وقعت في ألسنة أهل الخزي والخذلان، وثالثها: هو في أصله غير مبني على المنهج القويم والصراط المستقيم، وأن هذا الكتاب قد اتفقت له آفة أخرى، وهي أنه صغير الحجم، وفي اعتقاد الجمهور أنه كثير العلم.

فرحمك الله يا إمام أهل السنة، ما أعظمك إماما، وإن رماك أهل الجهل بكل شنيعة هي بنفوسهم قائمة قيام الصفة بالموصوف، ولا يستدل بها إلا على»

(1) نقلت هذا النص عن مقدمة د/ عبد الرحمن بدوي لتحقيقه لكتاب عيون الحكمة.
Commentary on Sullam al-'Ulum by Bahr al-'Ulum.

Islam and the Rational Sciences.

There is no doubt that what these imams did is something that Allah Most High obligated upon them: to defend the sanctity of Islam and its sacredness and to strengthen the hearts of the believers in it. So they are not to be blamed at all; rather their efforts are eternally appreciated. And al-Taj al-Subki, we saw how he disliked Greek and Peripatetic philosophy, but we found him praising al-Ghazali and al-Razi, and likewise he praised al-Baydawi and al-Amidi and others who became immersed in the sciences of these philosophers, delved into them, and praised them, while he is the vigilant guardian of the creeds of the Muslims, who leaves no small or great matter that touches their dignity and purity except he records it; he never attacked these imams at all.

And the fame of the Sultan of Scholars, 'Izz al-Din ibn 'Abd al-Salam, spread as a jurist upon the path of the Salaf, and a cautious hadith scholar. No two differ regarding his imamate and the greatness of his rank. He was asked about his teacher Sayf al-Din al-Amidi, against whom the anthropomorphists increased their attacks for reasons, including his occupation with these sciences. So what was his reply to the question? He said: 'If a heretic emerges to demolish Islam, al-Amidi would be designated to refute him in this time.' And he is the one who walked in his funeral procession when al-Amidi died, and countless people walked with him.

And what must be noted here is that our Ash'ari imams, may Allah be pleased with them all, did not abandon Ash'arism and did not accuse it of backwardness after delving into those sciences full of the poisons of doubts and suspicious fancies, until they became imams pointed to by fingers in those arts. And it became very easy for them to boast over their Ash'ari brothers or to be arrogant towards them, to the extent that they would leave the school and attack it and its legacy and its imams. But none of that happened. Rather, each of them remained upon his adherence that he had before entering these sciences, not only in fundamentals but even in branches. Thus al-Razi is an Ash'ari Shafi'i to the core, and al-Amidi is an Ash'ari Shafi'i in his blood and flesh. This is firstly by success from Allah, secondly due to the fulfillment of the conditions that al-Taj al-Subki indicated in them, and thirdly due to their good intentions and pure aims: they serve the religion of Islam. So it is incumbent upon Allah, by His prior promise, to guide everyone who strives in His path.

And Ash'ari discourse was never an ally of Peripatetic philosophy, nor did our theological method take from it a companion or friend in any period of history. And the theologians of Ahl al-Sunnah were never committed to believing everything between the covers of "al-Shifa'" and "al-Isharat." Rather, war between the two methods has existed from the beginning until now. Look at the most wonderful thing said by the Sunni Ash'ari theologian on the tongue of Imam al-Razi, the pride of the community and religion, as he undertakes to explain 'Uyun al-Hikmah of Ibn Sina, explaining why he refrained from commenting on it until now, saying: 'I refrained from it for matters... Secondly: I am opposed to the requirement of this book in its subtle and clear, its general and details. If I would drag upon it the tail of leniency and flattery, I would become like one who is content with guiding people to the paths of error and corruption. And if I would gird myself for disclosure and clarification, I would fall into the tongues of the people of disgrace and abandonment. Thirdly: it is in its origin not built upon the upright methodology and the straight path, and that this book has befallen another affliction: it is small in size, and in the belief of the people it has much knowledge.

May Allah have mercy on you, O Imam of Ahl al-Sunnah! How great you are as an imam, even if the people of ignorance attack you with every slander that stands in their souls like the standing of the attribute in the described, and nothing is inferred from it except...'

(1) This text is quoted from the introduction of Dr. 'Abd al-Rahman Badawi in his critical edition of the book 'Uyun al-Hikmah.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is front matter from Bahr al-'Ulum's commentary on Sullam al-'Ulum, intended to justify the study of rational sciences (philosophy) by Ash'ari scholars. The author begins by asserting that such study was a religious obligation to defend Islam. He cites al-Taj al-Subki, who disliked Greek philosophy but praised scholars like al-Ghazali and al-Razi for engaging with it. Then he recounts an anecdote about Ibn 'Abd al-Salam defending al-Amidi against anthropomorphist critics. The author emphasizes that these imams never compromised their Ash'ari creed; they remained steadfast. He quotes al-Razi's own words from his introduction to 'Uyun al-Hikmah, where al-Razi explains his reluctance to write a commentary due to disagreement with Ibn Sina's philosophy. The passage ends with a supplication for al-Razi. The argumentative flow is: (1) Ash'ari imams engaged in rational sciences as a duty, (2) They were not blamed, (3) Despite their expertise, they remained loyal to Ash'arism, (4) Ash'ari theology is distinct from philosophy, as shown by al-Razi's critical stance. The examples are firmly rooted in Islamic scholarly history, including references to specific works like al-Shifa' and al-Isharat.

Key Terms
الأشعرية
الفلسفة المشائية
العلوم العقلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what reason did al-Razi give for hesitating to comment on Ibn Sina's 'Uyun al-Hikmah?
A) He lacked sufficient time and resources.
B) He feared criticism from the common people.
C) He disagreed with the book's content in both its general and precise details.
D) He found the book too obscure to understand.

Key Takeaway
Ash'ari scholars engaged in philosophy with clear intention and without abandoning their creed, distinguishing their approach as critical engagement rather than blind acceptance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify one key argument from the passage that supports the view that studying philosophy does not compromise Ash'ari creed.
?
Compare Bahr al-'Ulum's defense with the position of al-Ghazali in his 'Tahafut al-Falasifa.' How are they similar or different?

Al-Farabi and the Development of Islamic Logic
Author traces the historical stages of development of rational sciences in Islam, highlighting al-Farabi's foundational role.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe al-Farabi's definition of logic and his role as the first builder of philosophical sciences in Islam.

Core Idea
Al-Farabi, the Second Teacher, defined logic as a universal law of human expression.

This lesson explores the gradual development of rational sciences in Islam, focusing on the pivotal role of al-Farabi. Known as the 'Second Teacher' after Aristotle, he was the first to systematically build philosophical sciences, and he offered a unique definition of logic as a universal law of expression that progresses from simple to complex. Understanding his contribution provides a foundation for the later flourishing of logic in the Islamic world.

Guided Path
1
Identify the historical context
Note the author's description of the stages: in the 2nd/3rd centuries AH, Muslims translated foreign sciences; in the 4th century, they moved to independent production. Al-Farabi belongs to this later productive phase.
2
Extract al-Farabi's definition of logic
Find the exact phrase: 'a law of expression in the language of human reason among all nations'. Notice that it emphasizes universality and a progression from word to proposition to syllogism.
3
Explain the significance of his title
He is called 'the second teacher' after Aristotle, indicating his foundational role in building philosophical sciences in Islam. This title is unique to him.
4
Connect to later logic works
Al-Farabi's three-part structure (word, proposition, syllogism) became standard in later logic textbooks. This shows his lasting influence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث الثاني: تطور العلوم العقلية في الإسلام. لم يحدث التطور في تاريخ العلوم العقلية في الإسلام دفعة واحدة، وبصدفة ، وإنما حدث هذا التطور على مراحل مختلفة، كما أنه على درجات متفاوتة في العالم الإسلامي؛ حيث يختلف المشرق عن المغرب، ويتفاوت الأمر بين العرب والعجم. ويمكن أن يقال بوجه عام إذا كان المسلمون في القرنين الثاني والثالث للهجرة قد شغلوا بنقل العلوم الأجنبية وتفهمها، فإنهم كانوا في القرن الرابع يدرسون بأنفسهم ولأنفسهم، وانتقلوا من الجمع والتحصيل إلى الإنتاج. ويعد الفارابي أبو نصر أول القائمين بمهمة بناء العلوم الفلسفية في تاريخ الإسلام، وهو المعلم الثاني، نظر إلى المنطق على أنه «قانون للتعبير بلغة العقل الإنساني عند جميع الأمم، ولا بد أن يسير من أبسط عناصر الكلام إلى أعقدها: من الكلمة إلى القضية إلى القياس» ، ورأى أن المنطق
The second topic: The development of rational sciences in Islam. The development in the history of rational sciences in Islam did not occur all at once and by chance, but rather this development occurred in different stages, and it is also of varying degrees in the Islamic world; as the East differs from the West, and the matter varies between Arabs and non-Arabs. It can be said generally that if Muslims in the second and third centuries AH were occupied with translating and understanding foreign sciences, then in the fourth century they were studying by themselves and for themselves, and moved from gathering and acquisition to production. And al-Farabi Abu Nasr is considered the first to undertake the task of building the philosophical sciences in the history of Islam, and he is the second teacher. He viewed logic as 'a law of expression in the language of human reason among all nations, and it must proceed from the simplest elements of speech to the most complex: from the word to the proposition to the syllogism', and he saw that logic...
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage provides a historical overview of the development of rational sciences (including logic) in the Islamic world. The author notes that this development was gradual and varied regionally. He then highlights the pivotal role of al-Farabi, known as the 'Second Teacher' (after Aristotle), as the first to systematically build philosophical sciences in Islam. Al-Farabi's conception of logic is presented: he considered logic a universal law of human expression, progressing from the word (lafz) to the proposition (qadiyya) to the syllogism (qiyas). This reflects the structure of logic texts that begin with simple terms and build up to arguments. The passage ends abruptly, suggesting further discussion of al-Farabi's views on logic.

Key Terms
المعلم الثاني
المنطق

Key Takeaway
Al-Farabi, the Second Teacher, was the first to systematically build philosophical sciences in Islam and defined logic as a universal law of expression progressing from word to proposition to syllogism.

Al-Razi's Role in Rational Sciences
Author presents al-Razi's role in developing philosophy, logic, and kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's contributions to the rational sciences and name the scholars influenced by his school.

Core Idea
Al-Razi's school shaped the trajectory of Islamic rational sciences.

This passage introduces Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi as a pivotal figure in philosophy, logic, and kalam. It describes his school, followers, and critics, and lists his major works. Understanding this helps situate later developments in Islamic logic and theology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fields of contribution
Al-Razi contributed to philosophy (falsafa), logic (mantiq), and kalam (theology). Note the phrase 'al-ulum al-aqliyya' which includes these three.
These are the rational sciences as opposed to transmitted sciences.
2
Recognize his school and followers
Al-Razi founded a distinct school (madrasa) within the rational sciences. The passage mentions al-Baydawi, al-Urmawi, and al-Iji as following his method.
These scholars are known for their works in logic and kalam.
3
Note the criticism he faced
Not all accepted al-Razi's views; some scholars criticized and rejected his opinions. This shows scientific debate in the tradition.
4
List his major works
The passage names five key works: al-Mulakhkhas, al-Muhassal, al-Mabahith al-Mashriqiyya, Nihayat al-Uqul, and Sharh al-Isharat. These are considered landmarks.
These works cover logic, philosophy, and theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإسلام والعلوم العقلية ثم للإمام فخر الدين الرازي دور كبير في تطوير العلوم العقلية: فلسفة ومنطقا وكلاما وهو صاحب مدرسة فيها تتميز بمميزات وخصائص، جرى على إثره أمة من أهل العلم كالبيضاوي والأرموي والإيجي، كما لقي بعض آرائه واتجاهاته نقدا ورفضا من قبل طائفة أخرى. وما تركه الرازي من المؤلفات ، كـ «الملخص و المحصل» و«المباحث المشرقية» ونهاية العقول» و شرح الإشارات» وغيرها يمثل مرحلة فارقة في طريق التطور.
Islam and the Rational Sciences. Then Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi had a major role in developing the rational sciences: philosophy, logic, and kalam. He was the founder of a school in it characterized by distinct features and characteristics, followed by a nation of scholars like al-Baydawi, al-Urmawi, and al-Iji. Some of his opinions and directions also met criticism and rejection from another group. And what al-Razi left of authored works, such as al-Mulakhkhas, al-Muhassal, al-Mabahith al-Mashriqiyya, Nihayat al-Uqul, Sharh al-Isharat, and others, represents a decisive stage in the path of development.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a biographical overview of Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's impact on the rational sciences ('ulum 'aqliyya). It begins by highlighting his role in advancing philosophy (falsafa), logic (mantiq), and kalam (theology). The author notes that al-Razi established a distinct school that influenced scholars such as al-Baydawi, al-Urmawi, and al-Iji. However, some of his views faced opposition from other groups. The passage concludes by listing al-Razi's major works—al-Mulakhkhas, al-Muhassal, al-Mabahith al-Mashriqiyya, Nihayat al-Uqul, and Sharh al-Isharat—and asserts that these writings represent a pivotal stage in the evolution of rational thought. The commentary follows the author's order: first the role, then the school and its followers, then the criticism, and finally the significance of his writings.

مدرسة

Fakhr al-Din al-Razi was a major figure in the rational sciences whose school and writings influenced generations of scholars.

Al-Tusi's Tajrid and the Transformation of Kalam
Author describes al-Tusi's Tajrid as pivotal in mixing philosophy with kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key transformation al-Tusi's Tajrid al-'Aqa'id brought to kalam and name the later mutakallimun who followed his logical arrangement.

Core Idea
Al-Tusi made philosophy and kalam one, forever changing Islamic theology.

This lesson presents a key turning point in the history of Islamic thought: Nasir al-Din al-Tusi's Tajrid al-'Aqa'id. The passage you will read explains how this work integrated philosophy into kalam for the first time, and how its logical arrangement of topics became the standard for later theologians. Understanding this transformation will help you see why kalam texts after al-Tusi have a distinctly philosophical and systematic structure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and work
Find the name of the scholar and the title of his book in the Arabic passage. Note that the work is called Tajrid al-'Aqa'id.
2
Understand the main claim
The passage says this book was pivotal because it 'mixed philosophy for the first time in Islam with kalam completely.' Grasp that this was a transformative merger, not a mere addition.
3
Recognize the impact on later scholars
The passage names three later mutakallimun—al-'Adud, al-Sa'd, al-Sayyid—who followed al-Tusi's logical order of topics. Memorize these names as examples of post-Tajrid kalam writers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُعد النصير الطوسي ممن ترك أثرا وضاحا في مسيرة هذا التطور ؛ حيث ألف كتابه تجريد العقائد»، الذي يعتبره البعض الكتاب الفاصل في تحويل مجرى الأبحاث الكلامية إلى الطابع الفلسفي، ابتداء من نهاية القرن السابع الهجري/ الثالث عشر الميلادي»، ويفسر سبب ذلك بأنه «مزج فيه الفلسفة لأول مرة في الإسلام بعلم الكلام مزجا تاما، بحيث صارا شيئا واحدا. كما أن لكتابه هذا أثرا بالغا في ترتيب موضوات علم الكلام، حيث جرى من جاء بعده من المتكلمين على منواله في ترتيبها كالعضد والسعد والسيد، والكتب الكلامية قبله لم يوجد فيها هذا الترتيب المنطقي المتسق مع طبيعة التفكير المنهجي، يعرف ذلك من قارن بين هذا الكتاب وكتب هؤلاء مقارنة سريعة .
Al-Nasir al-Tusi is considered among those who left a clear impact on the course of this development; for he authored his book Tajrid al-'Aqa'id, which some consider the pivotal book in diverting the course of kalam research towards a philosophical character, starting from the end of the 7th century AH/13th century CE. The reason for this is that 'he mixed philosophy for the first time in Islam with kalam completely, such that they became one thing.' Also, this book had a profound effect on ordering the topics of kalam, as those who came after him among the mutakallimun followed his pattern in arranging them, such as al-'Adud, al-Sa'd, and al-Sayyid. Kalam books before him did not have this logical arrangement consistent with the nature of systematic thinking, as is known by those who compare this book with the books of these scholars quickly.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a biographical notice on Nasir al-Din al-Tusi and his seminal work Tajrid al-'Aqa'id. The author begins by stating that al-Tusi left a clear impact, then explains that his book is considered a turning point because it fully integrated philosophy into kalam for the first time. The passage quotes a reason: philosophy and kalam became one. Next, the author discusses the book's influence on the arrangement of kalam topics, noting that later mutakallimun like al-'Adud al-Din al-Iji (al-'Adud), al-Sa'd al-Taftazani, and al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani followed his ordering. The passage emphasizes that pre-Tajrid kalam works lacked this logical and systematic arrangement. The commentary follows the author's sequence: impact, reason, effect on later scholars.

Al-Taftazani and al-Jurjani: Editors of Rational Sciences
Author compares al-Taftazani and al-Jurjani to al-Rafi'i and al-Nawawi for rational sciences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the role of al-Taftazani and al-Jurjani in the development of rational sciences and list their major works.

Core Idea
Al-Taftazani and al-Jurjani are the al-Rafi'i and al-Nawawi of rational sciences.

Just as al-Rafi'i and al-Nawawi systematized and edited the Shafi'i school in fiqh, al-Taftazani and al-Jurjani performed a similar tahrir (critical editing) for the rational sciences (al-‘ulūm al-‘aqliyya). Their works became indispensable references for later scholars. This lesson introduces you to their role and their key texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the comparison
Find the analogy: al-Taftazani and al-Jurjani are to rational sciences as al-Rafi'i and al-Nawawi are to fiqh. What does this tell you about the nature of their contribution?
The comparison emphasizes the systematic editing and canonization of the field.
2
List the major works
From the passage, list at least five works mentioned. Note which are by al-Taftazani (e.g., al-Maqasid, al-Tahdhib, al-Talwih) and which by al-Jurjani (e.g., Sharh al-Mawaqif, Hashiyat Sharh al-Mukhtasar al-'Adudi).
The passage groups their works together; use secondary knowledge if needed, but the main list is from the text.
3
Recognize al-Dawani's role
After the two imams, the passage mentions Jalal al-Din al-Dawani and his three glosses on the new commentary on al-Tajrid. How does he fit chronologically and conceptually?
Al-Dawani represents the next generation of commentators, building on their tahrir.
4
Assess the significance
Why does the author say these works are indispensable for studying the development of rational sciences? What does it mean for a text to be part of the 'tahrir' stage?
These works consolidate and clarify earlier debates, forming the core curriculum for later scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم تفقد العلوم العقلية رجالا قاموا بالتحرير للمسائل والقضايا العقلية ، ولئن كان مرحلة الإمامين الرافعي والنووي مرحلة تحرير المذهب الشافعي في الفقه فإن مرحلة سعد الدين التفتازاني والسيد الشريف الجرجاني مرحلة تحرير المسائل العقلية في الإسلام وهما بمثابة الرافعي والنووي، ومؤلفاتهما كالمقاصد وشرحه، وشرح الشمسية والتهذيب والتلويح، وحاشية شرح المختصر للسعد وشرح المواقف، وحاشية شرح القطب على الشمسية، وشرحه على المطالع ، وحاشية شرح المختصر العضدي للسيد ـ لا يستغني عنها جميعا كل من أراد دراسة تطور العلوم العقلية. ويأتي بعدهما مباشرة دور المحقق جلال الدين الدواني، صاحب الحواشي الثلاثة المعروفة ـ القديمة ، الجديدة، الأجدـ على الشرح الجديد على التجريد، وغيرها من الحواشي والتعليقات والرسائل.
The rational sciences did not lack men who undertook the editing of rational issues and questions. And if the stage of the two Imams al-Rafi'i and al-Nawawi was the stage of editing the Shafi'i school in fiqh, then the stage of Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani and al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani was the stage of editing the rational sciences in Islam. The two are like al-Rafi'i and al-Nawawi, and their works—such as al-Maqasid and its commentary, Sharh al-Shamsiyya, al-Tahdhib, al-Talwih, Hashiyat Sharh al-Mukhtasar for al-Sa'd, Sharh al-Mawaqif, Hashiyat Sharh al-Qutb on al-Shamsiyya, his commentary on al-Matali', and Hashiyat Sharh al-Mukhtasar al-'Adudi for al-Sayyid—all of them are indispensable for anyone who wants to study the development of the rational sciences. Immediately after them comes the role of the researcher Jalal al-Din al-Dawani, author of the three famous commentaries—the old, the new, and the newest—on the new commentary on al-Tajrid, and other glosses, commentaries, and treatises.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a biographical comparison highlighting the roles of al-Taftazani and al-Jurjani in rational sciences. The author parallels their editing (tahrir) of rational sciences with al-Rafi'i and al-Nawawi's editing of Shafi'i fiqh. Then a list of their major works is provided, emphasizing their indispensability for studying the development of rational sciences. The passage ends by mentioning al-Dawani's subsequent contributions with his three glosses on the new commentary on al-Tajrid. The commentary follows the author's order: first the comparison, then the works, then al-Dawani.

Key Terms

الحواشي

Al-Taftazani and al-Jurjani systematically edited rational sciences, and their works, alongside al-Dawani's glosses, form the core post-classical curriculum in kalam and logic.

Later Commentators of Rational Sciences
Author compares later commentators' efforts to those of Shafi'i jurists.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three later commentators mentioned (al-Salkuti, al-Bihari, al-Harawi) and match each to their major works.

Core Idea
Later commentators built upon earlier rational sciences, mirroring the work of Shafi'i jurists.

In the history of Islamic logic and kalam, certain scholars stand out for their glosses and commentaries that clarified and expanded earlier texts. This passage introduces three such figures from a later stage and compares their contributions to those of renowned Shafi'i jurists. Understanding these scholarly chains helps you trace the development of ideas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scholars
Read the Arabic and find the names: 'Abd al-Hakim al-Salkuti, Muhibb Allah al-Bihari, and Mir Muhammad Zahid al-Harawi. Note the honorifics used (al-`allama, al-imam, al-muhaqqiq).
2
Match each scholar to his works
The passage lists: al-Salkuti wrote glosses on Sharh al-Shamsiyya, al-Mawaqif, and al-Khayali; al-Bihari authored al-Sullam and al-Muslim; al-Harawi wrote commentaries on al-Dawani, al-Qutb, and al-Sayyid al-Sharif. Commit these to memory.
These are standard texts in logic and kalam.
3
Understand the comparison to Shafi'i jurists
The author parallels these three with Ibn Hajar al-Haytami, al-Khatib al-Shirbini, and al-Shams al-Ramli. This shows that the growth of rational sciences mirrors the development of fiqh.
Recognizing such parallels aids in memorizing scholarly chains.
4
Recognize the role of glossators (muhashshin)
The passage ends by praising all commentators—major, middle, minor—for their service to the rational sciences. This highlights the collective effort in transmitting and refining knowledge.

Then comes the role of the commentators and glossators, among them the major, middle, and minor, each having efforts and services to the precious rational sciences that are thanked and remembered. May Allah reward them all for the effort and exertion they bore in fulfilling the trust of conveying the word.

Understanding Al-'Attar's Defense of Later Scholars' Excellence
Author highlights India's eminence in intellectual sciences and cites al-'Attar's defense of later scholars' excellence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain al-'Attar's argument that later scholars can achieve excellence despite a general decline in virtues over time.

Core Idea
God's grace is continuous; individual later scholars can surpass earlier ones.

The author of Bahr al-Ulum asserts India's eminence in intellectual sciences and supports it by citing Shaykh al-Islam Hasan al-'Attar's commentary on al-Taj al-Subki. Al-'Attar addresses a common objection: if time itself diminishes virtue, how can later scholars produce works of equal or greater excellence? His response provides a nuanced understanding of scholarly progress by distinguishing between general decline and individual achievement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Problem
Al-Mahalli restricted the excellence of al-Subki's book to al-Subki's own time, implying later people cannot match it. What logical issue does this raise for later scholars?
This restriction is called 'taqyid bi-zaman al-musannif'.
2
Extract Al-'Attar's Premise
Al-'Attar argues that God's grace is vast and does not cease. This means that later scholars can also receive divine gifts enabling excellence.
He says: 'فإن فضل الله واسع، ومواهب الحق سبحانه لا تنقطع عن العباد'
3
Address the Counterargument
A common counterargument is that time itself decreases in virtues. Al-'Attar acknowledges this but makes a crucial distinction.
4
Recognize the Key Distinction
The decrease in virtues applies to the entire class (al-tabaqa) as a whole, not necessarily to every individual. Therefore, individual later scholars can still surpass earlier ones.
He says: 'تناقصه بالنسبة لمجموع الطبقة، فلا ينافي تفوق بعض أفراد من المتأخرة على ما قبلها'
5
Connect to Al-Subki's Acknowledgment
Al-'Attar notes that even al-Subki himself acknowledged this possibility in his introduction, so the point is not new.
This strengthens the argument by showing it is not a novel claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني نصيب الهند في العلوم العقلية. في هذا الفصل أريد الإشارة إلى عظمة الهند في هذا المجال العلمي، وسبقها على كثير من الأقطار الإسلامية، في تخصيب الفكر الديني الإسلامي، وتميزها عن غيرها في كثرة الإنتاج والمبدعين فيه. هذا أمر اعترف به العارفون ، وإن لم يدركه القاصرون، فهاك نصا صريحا يدل باختصار على منزلة علماء الهند في العلوم العقلية، وهو لشيخ الإسلام حسن العطار رحمة الله ؛ حيث يقول معلقا على كلام التاج السبكي إن كتابه جمع الجوامع لا يمكن » اختصاره لأهل الزمان لبلوغه الغاية في الإتقان والإحكام، وقيده شارحه المحلي بأهل زمان التاج السبكي، علق عليه العطار قائلا: تقييده بزمان المصنف يقتضي أنه يأتي به من تأخر عن زمانه، ولا مانع ؛ فإن فضل الله واسع، ومواهب الحق سبحانه لا تنقطع عن العباد فيضانها والله ذو الفضل العظيم، ولا يناقض ما قلناه أن الزمان يتناقص في الفضائل كلما تقدم ؛ لأن تناقصه بالنسبة لمجموع الطبقة، فلا ينافي تفوق بعض أفراد من المتأخرة على ما قبلها، كما اعترف بذلك المصنف في خطبة
Chapter Two: India's Share in the Intellectual Sciences. In this chapter I wish to indicate the greatness of India in this scientific field, and its precedence over many Islamic countries in enriching Islamic religious thought, and its distinction over others in the abundance of production and innovators therein. This is a matter recognized by the knowers, even if the deficient do not perceive it. Here is a clear text that briefly indicates the status of the scholars of India in the intellectual sciences, and it is from Shaykh al-Islam Hasan al-'Attar (may God have mercy on him) where he says, commenting on the statement of al-Taj al-Subki that his book 'Jami' al-Jawami' cannot be summarized for the people of the time due to its reaching the utmost perfection and precision, and his commentator al-Mahalli restricted it to the people of the time of al-Taj al-Subki. Al-'Attar commented saying: 'His restriction to the author's time implies that whoever comes after his time also attains it, and there is no hindrance; for God's grace is vast, and the gifts of the Truth (Exalted) do not cease from the servants in their outpouring, and God is the possessor of immense bounty. And what we have said does not contradict that time decreases in virtues as it advances; because its decrease is relative to the entire class, so it does not preclude the superiority of some individuals from later times over what came before, as the author acknowledged in his introduction.'
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage begins the second chapter, focusing on India's contribution to intellectual sciences. The author asserts India's greatness and precedence in enriching Islamic religious thought. To support this, he quotes Shaykh al-Islam Hasan al-'Attar, who comments on a statement by al-Taj al-Subki and his commentator al-Mahalli. Al-'Attar argues that restricting al-Subki's book to his own time does not prevent later scholars from producing works of similar excellence, because God's grace is continuous. He also clarifies that the general decline of virtue over time does not preclude individual later scholars from surpassing earlier ones, as the original author himself acknowledged.

Key Terms
تقييده بزمان المصنف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the decrease is only apparent.
B) Because the decrease applies to the group, not necessarily to every individual.
C) Because later scholars have more resources.
D) Because al-Mahalli's restriction was incorrect.

Key Takeaway
Later scholars can surpass earlier ones because God's grace is continuous, and general decline does not eliminate individual excellence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Write a short paragraph applying al-'Attar's reasoning to that area.

Layers of Scholarly Commentary
Author quotes al-ʿAṭṭār's commentary on al-Maḥalli's restriction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the different layers of commentary in a scholarly text and determine how each commentator builds on or responds to the previous one.

Core Idea
Scholarly commentary creates a chain of interpretation where each layer adds context or critique.

When studying classical Islamic texts, you often encounter multiple layers of commentary. In this passage, we see three levels: Taj al-Subki's original claim, al-Maḥalli's restriction, and al-ʿAṭṭār's response. Understanding how these layers interact helps you grasp the evolution of scholarly discourse and evaluate the strength of arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text claim
Locate the original statement by Taj al-Subki about his book Jamʿ al-Jawamiʿ. What did he claim about its abridgment?
The base text says the book cannot be abridged because it has reached perfection.
2
Find the first commentary layer
Al-Maḥalli added a restriction: he limited the understanding of the book to the people of Taj al-Subki's time. Why might he have done this?
This restriction implies a potential limitation on later scholars.
3
Extract the second commentary layer (al-ʿAṭṭār)
Hasan al-ʿAṭṭār responds to both. He argues that the restriction actually implies later scholars can come, because God's bounty is continuous. Analyze how his response challenges the implied limitation.
Al-ʿAṭṭār uses the restriction to defend the possibility of later excellence.
4
Assess the commentary chain's effect
How does al-ʿAṭṭār's commentary change the meaning of the base text? Does it strengthen or weaken the original claim?
It transforms a potential criticism into a positive argument for ongoing scholarly achievement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في هذا الفصل أريد الإشارة إلى عظمة الهند في هذا المجال العلمي، وسبقها على كثير من الأقطار الإسلامية، في تخصيب الفكر الديني الإسلامي، وتميزها عن غيرها في كثرة الإنتاج والمبدعين فيه. هذا أمر اعترف به العارفون، وإن لم يدركه القاصرون، فهاك نصا صريحا يدل باختصار على منزلة علماء الهند في العلوم العقلية، وهو لشيخ الإسلام حسن العطار رحمة الله؛ حيث يقول معلقا على كلام التاج السبكي إن كتابه جمع الجوامع لا يمكن اختصاره لأهل الزمان لبلوغه الغاية في الإتقان والإحكام، وقيده شارحه المحلي بأهل زمان التاج السبكي، علق عليه العطار قائلا: تقييده بزمان المصنف يقتضي أنه يأتي به من تأخر عن زمانه، ولا مانع؛ فإن فضل الله واسع، ومواهب الحق سبحانه لا تنقطع عن العباد فيضانها والله ذو الفضل العظيم، ولا يناقض ما قلناه أن الزمان يتناقص في الفضائل كلما تقدم؛ لأن تناقصه بالنسبة لمجموع الطبقة، فلا ينافي تفوق بعض أفراد من المتأخرة على ما قبلها، كما اعترف بذلك المصنف في خطبة ترشيح التوشيح.
In this chapter I wish to allude to the greatness of India in this scientific field, and its precedence over many Islamic regions in fertilizing Islamic religious thought, and its distinction from others in abundance of production and innovators therein. This is a matter acknowledged by the knowers, even if the deficient do not grasp it. So here is an explicit text that indicates briefly the station of the scholars of India in the rational sciences, and it is from Shaykh al-Islam Hasan al-ʿAṭṭār, may God have mercy on him, where he says, commenting on the words of Taj al-Subki that his book Jamʿ al-Jawamiʿ cannot be abridged for the people of the time because it has reached the ultimate in perfection and precision, and its commentator al-Maḥalli restricted it to the people of the time of Taj al-Subki. Al-ʿAṭṭār commented, saying: 'His restriction to the time of the author implies that one will come after his time, and there is no obstacle; for the bounty of God is vast, and the gifts of the Truth, glorified be He, never cease from the servants in their overflow. God is the possessor of great bounty. And what we have said does not contradict that time decreases in virtues as it advances; because its decrease is relative to the entire stratum, so it does not preclude the superiority of some individuals from the later ones over those before them, as the author himself acknowledged in the introduction of Tarshīḥ al-Tawshīḥ.'
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is an introduction to the chapter on India's contribution to rational sciences. The author begins by asserting the greatness of India in this field and its precedence over many Islamic regions, emphasizing the abundance of intellectual production and innovators. He states that this is a fact recognized by knowledgeable people, even if those of limited understanding do not perceive it. To support his claim, he quotes a clear text from Shaykh al-Islam Hasan al-ʿAṭṭār, who comments on Taj al-Subki's statement about his book Jamʿ al-Jawamiʿ. Al-ʿAṭṭār explains that when al-Maḥalli restricted the understanding of the book to the people of Taj al-Subki's time, it implies that later scholars may come who can also comprehend it, because God's bounty is continuous. He argues that the general decrease in virtues over time does not preclude exceptional individuals from later periods surpassing earlier ones. This is a defense of the possibility of later scholars achieving excellence, against the notion of inevitable decline.

Key Terms
التعليق
التقييد
الاختصار
طبقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Hasan al-ʿAṭṭār argue that al-Maḥalli's restriction actually supports the possibility of later scholars understanding Jamʿ al-Jawamiʿ?
A) Because the restriction implies that someone after Taj al-Subki's time can come and understand it.
B) Because al-Maḥalli said the book is easy for any time.
C) Because Taj al-Subki himself said later scholars would surpass him.
D) Because the book was written in a universal language.

Key Takeaway
A commentator can reinterpret a restriction as a positive affirmation of future scholarly potential.

The Possibility of Intellectual Excellence in Later Times
Al-ʿAṭṭār's argument about decline and individual excellence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct al-ʿAṭṭār's argument that later scholars can surpass earlier ones and evaluate its logical structure.

Core Idea
General decline does not preclude individual excellence.

A common trope in Islamic intellectual history is that early generations were superior (khayr al-qurūn). However, this passage presents a nuanced counterargument by Hasan al-ʿAṭṭār: while the overall level may decline, exceptional individuals can still emerge later. This lesson breaks down the logical form of that argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opposing view
What claim is al-ʿAṭṭār responding to? He mentions the idea that 'time decreases in virtues as it advances' (الزمان يتناقص في الفضائل كلما تقدم). This is the view he must reconcile with the possibility of later excellence.
This view is based on a hadith about the best generations being the earliest.
2
Extract al-ʿAṭṭār's distinction
He introduces a crucial distinction: the decrease is relative to the entire stratum (بمجموع الطبقة), not to every individual. Find the Arabic phrase: 'لأن تناقصه بالنسبة لمجموع الطبقة'.
This distinction allows individual exceptions to the general trend.
3
Formalize the argument as a conditional
We can represent it: If the decrease is only in the average of the stratum, then it does not preclude some individuals from being superior. This is a valid logical move. Identify the antecedent and consequent.
Antecedent: decrease is relative to entire stratum. Consequent: individual superiority is not precluded.
4
Check the argument's validity
Does the conclusion follow? If the average declines, it is still possible for a later individual to be above the old average. So the reasoning is sound. This is modus ponens: if P then Q; P is true, so Q is true.
The argument is logically valid, but its truth depends on the correctness of the premise about the nature of decline.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في هذا الفصل أريد الإشارة إلى عظمة الهند في هذا المجال العلمي، وسبقها على كثير من الأقطار الإسلامية، في تخصيب الفكر الديني الإسلامي، وتميزها عن غيرها في كثرة الإنتاج والمبدعين فيه. هذا أمر اعترف به العارفون، وإن لم يدركه القاصرون، فهاك نصا صريحا يدل باختصار على منزلة علماء الهند في العلوم العقلية، وهو لشيخ الإسلام حسن العطار رحمة الله؛ حيث يقول معلقا على كلام التاج السبكي إن كتابه جمع الجوامع لا يمكن اختصاره لأهل الزمان لبلوغه الغاية في الإتقان والإحكام، وقيده شارحه المحلي بأهل زمان التاج السبكي، علق عليه العطار قائلا: تقييده بزمان المصنف يقتضي أنه يأتي به من تأخر عن زمانه، ولا مانع؛ فإن فضل الله واسع، ومواهب الحق سبحانه لا تنقطع عن العباد فيضانها والله ذو الفضل العظيم، ولا يناقض ما قلناه أن الزمان يتناقص في الفضائل كلما تقدم؛ لأن تناقصه بالنسبة لمجموع الطبقة، فلا ينافي تفوق بعض أفراد من المتأخرة على ما قبلها، كما اعترف بذلك المصنف في خطبة ترشيح التوشيح.

This is a matter acknowledged by the knowers, even if the deficient do not grasp it. God is the possessor of great bounty. Refuting Claims About Scholarly Uniqueness
Author refutes a claim by impossibility and counterexamples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how a claim based on exhaustive survey is refuted using the impossibility argument and concrete counterexamples from Islamic scholarship.

Core Idea
Claims of uniqueness often rely on impossible exhaustive surveys.

This passage demonstrates a method of refutation: when someone claims no later scholar matched a certain work, the refutation can show that such a claim requires a complete survey of all scholars, which is impossible, and then provide specific counterexamples of later scholars who produced comparable or greater works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being refuted
Find the assertion that the author is challenging. In this passage, it is the claim that 'no one from the people of the author's time produced its like' (i.e., a work like Jamʿ al-Jawāmiʿ).
The claim is about uniqueness of a work by Taj al-Subki.
2
Understand the refutation strategy: impossibility of exhaustive survey
The author argues that proving such a claim requires a complete survey (istiqrāʾ tāmm) of all scholars of that age, which is practically impossible (mutʿasir بل mutʿadhdhir). Therefore, the claim is likely exaggeration (mubālagha).
This is a logical point: universal negative claims are hard to prove without exhaustive enumeration.
3
Recognize the use of counterexamples
The author then provides specific later scholars and works: al-Fanari's Fuṣūl al-Badāʾiʿ fī al-Uṣūl, and the Indian scholar's Musallam al-Thubūt and Sullam al-ʿUlūm, showing that later scholars not only matched but produced influential works.
Counterexamples directly refute the claim by showing instances that contradict it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على أن عدم إتيان أحد من أهل زمان المصنف بمثله قد يُمنع؛ لأنه يتوقف على استقراء أحوال العلماء الموجودين في ذلك العصر، وهو متعسر بل متعذر، وأمثال هذا الكلام يحمل على المبالغة، وقد ألف العلامة الفناري، المصنف، كتاب فصول البدائع في الأصول، وجمع فيه ما تفرق في كتب كثيرة، مع مزيد التحرير، وكثرة الفوائد، مما خلا عنها هذا الكتاب. وألف بعض علماء الهند كتابا في هذا العلم، وسماه «مسلم الثبوت»، و تاريخ تأليف هذا الكتاب هو اسمه، وهو ألف ومائة وتسع [١١٠٩هـ]، فهذا زمان متأخر عن المصنف. ومسلم الثبوت هذا قد اعتنى به كثير من الهند وما وراء النهر، ووضعوا عليه شروحا وحواشي، واشتغلوا به كاشتغال أهل ديارنا بهذا الكتاب [يقصد جمع الجوامع] إلى الآن، كما أخبرني بذلك بعض من لقيته من علماء الهند وعلماء ما وراء النهر. ولصاحب «مسلم الثبوت» كتاب جليل في المنطق سماه «سلم العلوم»، وشرحه جماعة من علماء الهند واعتنت به فضلاء تلك الديار، كاعتنائهم بـ«مسلم الثبوت»، وقد اطلعت له على شرحين، ونقلت عنهما في حاشيتي على الخبيصي.
Moreover, the claim that no one from the people of the author's time produced its like may be refuted; because it depends on surveying the conditions of scholars existing in that age, which is difficult, indeed impossible. Such statements are usually taken as exaggeration. Indeed, the scholar al-Fanari, the author, wrote the book Fuṣūl al-Badāʾiʿ fī al-Uṣūl, and gathered in it what was scattered in many books, with increased refinement and many benefits that this book lacks. And some scholar of India authored a book in this science and named it Musallam al-Thubūt, and the date of its composition is its name, i.e., 1109 [AH]. So this is a time later than the author. And this Musallam al-Thubūt was much attended to by many in India and Transoxiana. They wrote commentaries and glosses on it and engaged with it as the people of our lands engage with this book [i.e., Jamʿ al-Jawāmiʿ] until now, as informed by some scholars of India and Transoxiana whom I met. And the author of Musallam al-Thubūt also has a great book in logic called Sullam al-ʿUlūm, on which a group of Indian scholars wrote commentaries, and the learned of those lands attended to it as they attended to Musallam al-Thubūt. I have seen two commentaries on it and have quoted from them in my gloss on al-Khabīṣī.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage continues the defense of later scholars. The author challenges the claim that no one from Taj al-Subki's time produced a work like Jamʿ al-Jawāmiʿ, arguing that such a claim is based on a comprehensive survey of all scholars of that age, which is practically impossible, and such statements are usually hyperbole. He then provides evidence: the scholar al-Fanari wrote Fuṣūl al-Badāʾiʿ fī al-Uṣūl, which collected scattered materials with additional refinement and benefits. He also mentions an Indian scholar who authored Musallam al-Thubūt, dated 1109 AH (clearly later than Taj al-Subki). This work received much attention in India and Transoxiana, with many commentaries and glosses. Furthermore, the same author wrote a significant logic text called Sullam al-ʿUlūm, which also attracted commentaries. The author personally saw two commentaries on it and used them in his own gloss on al-Khabīṣī's commentary on logic. This demonstrates that later scholars not only matched but produced substantial works.

Key Terms
استقراء (survey)
استقراء تام (complete survey)
مبالغة (exaggeration)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the author's primary logical argument against the claim that no one after Taj al-Subki produced a work like Jamʿ al-Jawāmiʿ?
A) The claim is based on an impossible exhaustive survey of all scholars of that age.
B) He provides many counterexamples to disprove the claim.
C) He says the claim is true but exaggerated.
D) He argues that Taj al-Subki's work is actually not that great.

Key Takeaway
When a claim requires an impossible exhaustive survey to verify, it can be refuted on that basis, and concrete counterexamples further strengthen the refutation.

The Value of Later Scholars in Islam
Author praises two later scholars and their works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the scholarly contributions of ʿAbd al-Ḥakīm and Mīr Zāhid and explain why later scholars are respected in the Islamic tradition.

Core Idea
Later scholars can be as profound as early ones; their works command respect from the virtuous.

This passage from a classical logic textbook concludes a discussion by highlighting that exceptional scholars continue to emerge. The author specifically praises two later scholars, ʿAbd al-Ḥakīm and Mīr Zāhid, whose works earned widespread admiration. This lesson explores why such later authorities are valued and what their example teaches us about the continuity of Islamic scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Scholars
Locate the names mentioned: ʿAbd al-Ḥakīm and Mīr Zāhid. Note that they are described as 'rare talents' from the eleventh century.
Both are later scholars, not from the early generations.
2
Understand the Metaphor
The author says 'the necks of the virtuous have bowed' to their works. This metaphor indicates deep respect and humility before their scholarly achievements.
It implies that even the most learned acknowledged their superiority in certain matters.
3
Appreciate the Intellectual Challenge
The 'minds of the nobles boasted in grasping their subtleties' suggests that understanding their works required exceptional intellect. This reinforces the idea that later scholars produced original and complex ideas.
4
Connect to Broader Significance
The passage counters any notion that only early authorities matter. It shows that later scholars can produce works of lasting value, worthy of study and admiration in fields like fiqh, kalam, and logic.
This is an important principle for students of Islamic sciences: do not dismiss later scholarship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما زال الزمان يأتي بالنوادر هذا العلامة عبد الحكيم والعلامة مير زاهد، كلاهما ممن أدرك القرن الحادي عشر، ولهما من التأليف ما خضعت لها رقاب الفضلاء، وتفاخرت بإدراك دقائقها أذهان النبلاء.
And time continues to bring rare talents: this scholar ʿAbd al-Ḥakīm and the scholar Mīr Zāhid. Both are among those who lived in the eleventh century, and they composed works to which the necks of the virtuous have bowed, and the minds of the nobles have boasted in grasping their subtleties.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage concludes the chapter by emphasizing that time continues to produce exceptional scholars. The author specifically mentions two figures: ʿAbd al-Ḥakīm and Mīr Zāhid, both from the eleventh century. Their works were so profound that even the most virtuous scholars humbly acknowledged them, and the intellectually elite took pride in understanding their intricacies. This further supports the earlier argument that later generations can indeed produce outstanding scholars.

C) They ignored them.
D) They criticized them harshly.

Key Takeaway
Later scholars like ʿAbd al-Ḥakīm and Mīr Zāhid produced works that earned the admiration of the elite, proving that scholarly excellence is not confined to early generations.

The Earliest Islamic Contact with India
Author dates Islam's arrival in India to the Prophet's time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the historical claim that Islam entered India during the Prophet's era and distinguish it from later military conquests.

Core Idea
Islam's first arrival in India was before the conquests, through Companions.

Many assume that Islam reached India only with military expansion. But historians have traced an earlier, peaceful introduction during the Prophet's own lifetime. This lesson examines the evidence presented by the author and develops your ability to weigh such historical claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central claim
The author asserts that Islam entered India in the very era of prophethood. Locate this statement in the Arabic text and note the key phrase 'في عصر النبوة نفسه'.
2
Examine the evidence provided
The author cites a delegation of Companions arriving at the Malabar coast and building mosques. Ask: What kind of evidence is this? How does it support the claim?
3
Distinguish the two phases
The author then mentions military conquests from the north beginning in the 2nd century AH. Compare the two phases: one peaceful and early, the other later and by force.
4
Assess the historiographical method
The author says 'أثبتته الدراسات' (studies have established). Consider how historians use evidence like early mosque foundations to date the arrival of Islam in a region.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث الأول : بدايات الحركة العلمية في الهند: ومما أثبتته الدراسات أن دخول الإسلام في الهند كان في عصر النبوة نفسه؛ حيث وصل وفد من الصحابة رضوان الله عليهم إلى السواحل الهندية الجنوبية، المعروفة بـ مليبار) ، وأسسوا هناك عددا من المساجد، كانت مراكز الدعوة الإسلامية في عصرهم، وفيما يليه من العصور. كما أن الفتوحات العسكرية من جهة الشمال بدأت منذ القرن الثاني الهجري، حتى صار الحكم في الهند للمسلمين طوال أكثر من ثمانية قرون. ولا عجب في أن يصنع الإسلام في الهند العجائب، ويبني حضارة لم تكن تخطر ببال شعوبها، فالتاريخ الإسلامي يحدثنا عن أعلام وشخصيات في هذا البلد العريق، قدموا خدمات وتضحيات في نشر العلوم الدينية وتطوير الفنون العربية، كالتفسير والحديث والفقه والفتاوي واللغة والأدب، لا يقل عما قام به إخوانهم في سائر الأقطار الإسلامية. دورهم وأما عدد أعيان الهند في العلوم العقلية - الكلام والأصول والمنطق والفلسفة، وكذلك التصوف - فلا يكاد يدخل تحت الحصر والإحصاء، وقد يكون الإعراض عنهم هو الأنسب في مثل هذا المقام. وهل هناك أحد لا يعرف
The first topic: The beginnings of the scientific movement in India: Among what studies have established is that the entry of Islam into India was in the very era of prophethood; as a delegation of the Companions, may God be pleased with them, arrived at the southern Indian coasts, known as Malabar, and established there a number of mosques, which were centers of Islamic da'wa in their time and in subsequent eras. Likewise, military conquests from the north began from the second century AH, until Muslim rule in India lasted for more than eight centuries. And no wonder that Islam performed wonders in India and built a civilization that never occurred to its peoples. Islamic history tells us of eminent figures and personalities in this ancient land who rendered services and sacrifices in spreading religious sciences and developing Arabic arts, such as tafsir, hadith, fiqh, fatwas, language, and literature, no less than what their brethren in other Islamic lands did. Their role... As for the number of Indian notables in the rational sciences – theology, principles of jurisprudence, logic, philosophy, and also Sufism – it can hardly be counted or enumerated, and perhaps ignoring them is most appropriate in such a context. And is there anyone who does not know...
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage opens a new section on the beginnings of the scientific movement in India. The author states that research has established that Islam entered India during the Prophet's own time when a delegation of Companions reached the southern coast (Malabar) and built mosques that served as centers for Islamic propagation. Later, military conquests from the north began in the 2nd century AH, leading to over eight centuries of Muslim rule. The author emphasizes the remarkable achievements of Indian Muslims in religious sciences like tafsir, hadith, fiqh, and language, as well as rational sciences like logic, philosophy, and theology. He notes that the number of scholars in these fields is beyond count. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the author's intent is to recognize the vast and early contributions of Indian scholars to Islamic civilization.

Key Terms

وفد الصحابة

The Indian Contribution to the Rational Sciences
Lists prominent Indian scholars of rational sciences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify key Indian scholars who contributed to the rational sciences and describe their contributions based on the passage.

Core Idea
Indian scholars created a distinct and prolific tradition in logic and rational sciences.

This passage introduces a list of eminent Indian scholars who advanced the rational sciences, particularly logic and the etiquette of debate. It demonstrates that the Indian subcontinent was not merely a passive recipient but an active producer of logical works, with contributions spanning centuries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the thematic phrase
The passage opens with 'نصيب الهند في العلوم العقلية' (The share of India in the rational sciences). This establishes that the list to follow is a demonstration of India's contribution to fields like logic, theology, and philosophy.
2
Recognize the scholars and their works
Each name in the list represents a scholar. Note those associated with specific works or epithets. For example, Abd al-Rashid al-Jawnpuri is identified as the author of al-Rashidiyya on the etiquette of debate, indicating his specialization.
Pay special attention to the scholars whose names are followed by a description; these often indicate their major contribution.
3
Categorize the scholars by period and specialization
The list spans from al-Biruni (11th century) to Ahmad Rida Khan (20th century). Some, like al-Siyalkoti, are known for glosses on logic and theology; others, like al-Jawnpuri, wrote original works on debate methodology.
Categorization helps appreciate the continuity and development of the tradition.
4
Connect to the broader Islamic tradition
These Indian scholars engaged with the same logical and theological debates as their counterparts in the Arab world, often commenting on or expanding classical texts. Their works form part of the standard curriculum in many South Asian madrasas.
5
Assess the significance of the list
The mere existence of such a list refutes the notion that Islamic logic stagnated after the classical period. It shows a vibrant, ongoing tradition in India that produced original works and commentaries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نصيب الهند في العلوم العقلية (٣) (٢) أبا الريحان البيروني، والعلامة الإمام الشيخ صفي الدين الهندي والمحقق الكبير عبد الحكيم السيالكوتي، والشيخ عبد الرشيد الجونفوري، صاحب الرشيدية في آداب البحث والمناظرة (ت: ١٠٨٣هـ)، والعلامة المحقق مير محمد زاهد الهروي، وأبو الحسنات عبد الحي اللكهنوي، والشيخ فضل إمام الخيرابادي، وابنه فضل حق الخيرابادي، والعلامة الإمام المجدد أحمد رضا خان البريلوي، وغيرهم.
The share of India in rational sciences: Abu al-Rayhan al-Biruni, and the esteemed Imam Sheikh Safi al-Din al-Hindi, and the great investigator Abd al-Hakim al-Siyalkoti, and Sheikh Abd al-Rashid al-Jawnpuri, author of al-Rashidiyya on the etiquette of inquiry and debate (d. 1083 AH), and the esteemed investigator Mir Muhammad Zahid al-Harawi, and Abu al-Hasanat Abd al-Hayy al-Lakhnawi, and Sheikh Fadl Imam al-Khayrabadi, and his son Fadl Haqq al-Khayrabadi, and the esteemed Imam and renewer Ahmad Rida Khan al-Barilawi, and others.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical enumeration of key figures who contributed to the rational sciences (particularly logic) in the Indian subcontinent. The author begins by stating 'the share of India in rational sciences', then lists nine scholars by name, sometimes with their famous works or honorifics. The list includes Abu al-Rayhan al-Biruni, the polymath who wrote on India; Safi al-Din al-Hindi, a scholar of usul and kalam; Abd al-Hakim al-Siyalkoti, known for his glosses on logical and theological works; Abd al-Rashid al-Jawnpuri, author of al-Rashidiyya on the etiquette of debate; Mir Muhammad Zahid al-Harawi; Abu al-Hasanat Abd al-Hayy al-Lakhnawi, a Hanafi scholar; Fadl Imam al-Khayrabadi and his son Fadl Haqq, both logicians; and Ahmad Rida Khan al-Barilawi, the famous renewer. Biography of Ahmad Rida Khan al-Birlawi: A Footnote Scholar
Footnote biography of Ahmad Rida Khan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract key biographical details from a scholarly footnote and assess its role in establishing the author's authority.

Core Idea
Biographical footnotes link the scholar's life to his work, grounding authority in personal piety and learning.

This passage is a typical biographical footnote found in Islamic commentaries, providing essential context about the author. Understanding such footnotes helps you evaluate the reliability and significance of the scholar and his works. Here, you will learn to identify the key elements that establish a scholar's credentials and influence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the full name and lineage
Look for the scholar's complete name, including his father and grandfather, and his regional affiliations (e.g., al-Hanafi, al-Birlawi, al-Hindi). This establishes his scholarly chain and school.
The name often includes place and madhhab.
2
Note the honorific titles
Titles like 'al-mujaddid' (renewer) and 'Imam Ahl al-Sunnah' indicate his stature. Understand that 'mujaddid' is a religious renewal role believed to appear every century.
These titles are not generic but specific to his standing.
3
List his major works and their subjects
Scan for titles of works. Here, al-Fatawa al-Ridawiyya shows expertise in fiqh; others refute Deobandi views, showing theological engagement. This reveals his scholarly range.
Works often indicate the areas of his authority.
4
Assess the geographical scope of influence
The passage mentions northern India, Pakistan, Bangladesh. Consider how this fits with the spread of his school and the reach of his writings.
Geographical influence helps gauge historical impact.
5
Understand the purpose of the footnote in the commentary
This biography appears as a footnote to introduce the author of the commentary being studied. It serves to establish credibility and connect the reader to the author's legacy.
Footnotes are not mere decorations; they serve a pedagogical function.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هو : الإمام العلامة الفاضل ، مجدد المائة الرابعة عشر ، أحمد رضا بن نقي على بن رضا على الأفغاني الحنفي البريلوي الهندي ، الملقب بـ «إمام أهل السنة»، و«أعلى حضرت». ولد عام ١٢٧٢هـ / ١٨٥٦م ، برع في العلم ، وفاق أقرانه في كثير من الفنون، ومؤلفاته في مختلف العلوم والفنون تبلغ ألف مؤلف على رواية بعض مترجميه. وكان أثره على أهل في شمال الهند وباكستان وبنغلاديش لايزال حيا باقيا، وهو يعيش في قلوبهم عزيزا كريما. ومن أشهر مؤلفاته: الفتاوى الرضوية في مجلدات كثيرة ضخمة، جد الممتار حاشية رد المحتار لابن عابدين في الفقه الحنفي، فتاوى الحرمين برجف ندوة المين، الدولة المكية بالمادة الغيبية، سبحان السبوح عن عيب كذب مقبوح ، ردا على الديوبندية المجوزين للكذب على الباري تعالى أنوار المنان في توحيد القرآن، المستند المعتمد بناء نجاة الأبد حاشية السنة على المعتقد المنتقد لفضل رسول البدايوني. توفي عام ١٣٤٠هـ / ١٩٢١م. انظر نزهة الخواطر لللكهنوي : ١١٨٠/٣ – ١١٨٢.
He is: the imam, the outstanding scholar, the renewer of the fourteenth century, Ahmad Rida ibn Naqi Ali ibn Rida Ali al-Afghani al-Hanafi al-Birlawi al-Hindi, titled 'Imam of Ahl al-Sunnah' and 'A'la Hadrat'. He was born in 1272 AH / 1856 CE, excelled in knowledge, surpassed his peers in many arts, and his works in various sciences and arts number a thousand according to some of his translators. His influence on the people of northern India, Pakistan, and Bangladesh remains alive and enduring, and he lives in their hearts as dear and noble. Among his most famous works: al-Fatawa al-Ridawiyya in many large volumes, Jidd al-Mumtar commentary on Radd al-Muhtar of Ibn Abidin in Hanafi fiqh, Fatawa al-Haramayn 'Barjaf Nadwat al-Min', al-Dawla al-Makkiyya bi al-Madda al-Ghaybiyya, Subhan al-Subbuh 'an 'Ayb Kadhib Maqbuh (a response to the Deobandis who permitted lying about God Almighty), Anwar al-Manan fi Tawhid al-Qur'an, al-Mustanad al-Mu'tamad Bina' Najat al-Abad commentary on al-Sunnah 'ala al-Mu'taqad al-Muntaqad li Fadl Rasul al-Badayuni. He died in 1340 AH / 1921 CE. See Nuzhat al-Khawatir by al-Lakhnawi: 3/1180-1182.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note on Ahmad Rida Khan al-Birlawi, included as a footnote in the commentary. It presents him as the renewer (mujaddid) of the 14th Islamic century, a leading Hanafi scholar from India, known as 'Imam of Ahl al-Sunnah' and 'A'la Hadrat'. The text details his birth year (1272 AH / 1856 CE), his scholarly excellence, and his prolific authorship, claiming a thousand works. It notes his continued influence in South Asia. It lists several of his prominent works, particularly in Hanafi fiqh (e.g., al-Fatawa al-Ridawiyya, a commentary on Radd al-Muhtar), theological refutations of the Deoband school, and works on tawhid and sunna. The passage concludes with his death year and a source reference. This informs the reader of the authority and context of the author of the commentary being studied.

Accessing Indian Rational Works and al-Attar's Correction
Historical reflection on manuscript transmission of Indian rational sciences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the challenges in transmitting Indian rational sciences to the Arab world and explain al-Attar's method for correcting corrupted manuscripts.

Core Idea
Indian rational works were rare; al-Attar's corrections preserved crucial texts for the Islamic tradition.

This passage from Bahr Ulum highlights a little-known aspect of Islamic intellectual history: the difficulty of transmitting rational sciences from India to the Arab world. Despite India's rich contributions, works like those of Mir Zahid al-Hindi were virtually inaccessible in Egypt, Syria, and the Maghreb. Shaykh al-Islam Hasan al-Attar's account of obtaining a correct copy of 'Abd al-Hakim's work illustrates the painstaking efforts required to ensure textual accuracy. Understanding this context helps us appreciate the fragility and value of manuscript transmission in the pre-print era.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context of Arab-Indian scholarly exchange
The author notes that despite India's leading role in rational sciences, the Arab world did not adequately access Indian works. He mentions his own decades-long attempts to bridge this gap.
Consider why rational sciences might be harder to transmit than transmitted sciences.
2
Identify the problem of manuscript corruption
Al-Attar states that all copies of 'Abd al-Hakim's work were corrupted (muḥarrafa). This is a major obstacle for reliable scholarship.
Manuscript corruption can arise from scribal errors, intentional alterations, or lack of authoritative exemplars.
3
Analyze al-Attar's solution: obtaining a correct copy
A virtuous man from Bukhara brought a very correct (ṣaḥīḥa jiddan) copy of 'Abd al-Hakim's work. Al-Attar used it to correct an Egyptian copy and relied on it for transmission.
This shows the importance of travel and personal networks in manuscript correction.
4
Recognize the broader significance for Islamic sciences
The author praises al-Attar as an exemplary Azhari Ash'ari scholar whose efforts restored al-Azhar's prestige. This highlights how manuscript correction is not merely technical but integral to preserving the Islamic intellectual heritage.
The passage also mentions other rare glosses by Mir Zahid al-Hindi that were similarly obtained.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نصيب الهند في العلوم العقلية في الكلام، فجاء مسلم الثبوت» - الذي يضارع جمع الجوامع»، على ما يصفه العطار - من بلد السرهندي والدهلوي! فلا نستطيع التخلص من هذه التناقضات العجيبة في ضوء هذه الدعوى الغريبة، إلا بالحكم عليها بأنها كاذبة لم تَنْبَنِ على أساس يثبت صدقها، بل مما اخترعتها عقولهم الماكرة ؛ ليروجوا بها بضاعتهم التي لولا مثلها لن تَجِدَ إلى رواجها سبيلا ، ولكن الله متم نوره ولو كره الملبسون . المبحث الرابع: الحوار العربي الهندي ومع هذا الدور القيادي للهند، إلا أن العالم العربي لم يدرك الهند كما ينبغي، ومن هنا كانت المحاولات التي بدأتُ في تكثيفها منذ سنوات عدة؛ حيث تتبعت نفائس الهند المكنونة، وجريت وراء كنوزها المخفية؛ لكي يتم بناء جسر ممدود يمكن العبور منه بين العالم العربي والبلاد الهندية، ويتسر الاطلاع على مساهمات علماء الهند في العلوم الدينية، لمن يعيش بعيدا عن هذه الديار ، لا للمهتمين الباحثين فقط ، بل لكل من يمكنه الارتياد لدور النشر والمكتبات في العالم العربي. وقد ساعدني الحظ في إخراج البعض المتعلق بالعلوم النقلية ، ولله الحمد والمنة. وأما نتاج الهند في العلوم العقلية فكان بعيد المنال جدا بالنسبة للعالم العربي، سيما الديار المصرية والشامية والعراقية، فضلا عن المغرب الإسلامي. وما كانت مؤلفات أهل الهند العقلية تصل إلى تلك الأقطار، وإن وصلت في حالات نادرة جدا وصلت على وجه غير مرضي. فانظر إلى هذا النص الرائع الذي حفظه لنا التاريخ ، سطره يراعة الإمام شيخ الإسلام حسن العطار رحمة الله ، يقول فيه في بعض المناسبات: ... وأصل نسخ عبد الحكيم كلها محرفة .. وقد منّ الله على الفقير بنسخة من عبد الحكيم صحيحة جدا، قدم بها رجل فاضل من بخاری، فصححنا عليها نسخة مصرية، وعليها اعتمدت في النقل ... ) . ويقول في موضع آخر : ورأيت للعلامة المحقق مير زاهد الهندي تحريرا نفيسا .. ربما لا يقف عليه غيري ؛ فإن حاشيته المذكورة وكذلك حاشيته على شرح الجلال الدواني.. وحاشيته على شرح الهياكل للدواني قدم بها رجل من علماء بخارى مصر، مريدا للحج، فحصلنا منه حاشية العلامة عبد الحكيم على المواقف، وصححنا نسخة مير زاهد على الدواني.. ولم يسمح بحواشي مير زاهد ولا بغيرها من بقية الكتب التي رأيناها معه، مما لا يوجد في بلادنا، بل كنا لا نعرف أسماءها فضلا عن مسمياتها" فسبحان من أحاط بكل شيء علما ، ورحم الله شيخنا العطار، فقد ضرب أروع مثال لعالم أزهري أشعري بمثله صارت للأزهر ما كان لها من الهيبة ، وإن مزقها أصحاب الدعاوي الفارغة بعده. (۱) حاشية العطار على الخبيصي: ۱۹۹. (۲) السابق: ۲۲۱
India's share in the rational sciences in theology: thus came 'Musallam al-Thubut' - which rivals 'Jam' al-Jawami'' - as al-Attar describes it - from the land of al-Sirhindi and al-Dehlawi! So we cannot rid ourselves of these wondrous contradictions in light of this strange claim, except by judging them as false, having been built on no basis proving their truth, but rather among what their cunning minds invented; to promote thereby their commodity, which without such [claims] would find no path to circulation. But Allah will perfect His light, though the falsifiers dislike it. The Fourth Topic: The Arab-Indian Dialogue. Despite this leading role of India, the Arab world did not realize India as it should; hence the attempts I began to intensify several years ago: I traced the hidden treasures of India and pursued its concealed riches, to build an extended bridge through which crossing is possible between the Arab world and the Indian lands, and to facilitate access to the contributions of Indian scholars in the religious sciences for those living far from these lands, not only for interested researchers but for anyone who can visit publishing houses and libraries in the Arab world. Luck has helped me in bringing out some related to the transmitted sciences, and to Allah is praise and gratitude. As for India's output in the rational sciences, it was very far out of reach for the Arab world, especially the Egyptian, Syrian, and Iraqi lands, let alone the Islamic Maghreb. The rational compositions of the people of India did not reach those regions, and if they did in very rare cases, they arrived in an unsatisfactory manner. So look at this wonderful text that history preserved for us, recorded by the pen of the Imam, Shaykh al-Islam Hasan al-Attar, may Allah have mercy on him. He says on some occasions: '...All the copies of 'Abd al-Hakim are corrupted... And Allah favored me by giving me a very correct copy of 'Abd al-Hakim, brought by a virtuous man from Bukhara; so we corrected an Egyptian copy with it, and upon it I relied in transmission...' And he says in another place: 'I saw for the accomplished investigator Mir Zahid al-Hindi a precious commentary... probably no one else has seen it; for his mentioned gloss, as well as his gloss on Sharh al-Jalal al-Dawwani, and his gloss on Sharh al-Hayakil by al-Dawwani, a man from the scholars of Bukhara brought them to Egypt, intending to perform Hajj, and we obtained from him the gloss of 'Allama 'Abd al-Hakim on al-Mawaqif, and we corrected Mir Zahid's copy with al-Dawwani... And he allowed neither Mir Zahid's gloss nor any other books we saw with him, which do not exist in our country; indeed we did not know their names, let alone what they designated.' So glory be to Him who encompasses all things with knowledge, and may Allah have mercy on our shaykh al-Attar, for he set the most wonderful example of an Azhari Ash'ari scholar, by whom al-Azhar regained the prestige it had, though the claimants of empty claims have torn it apart after him. (1) Attar's gloss on al-Khubaysi: 199. (2) Previous: 221.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a historical and methodological reflection by the author of Bahr Ulum on the scarcity of Indian rational sciences in the Arab world and the efforts to correct manuscripts. The author begins by noting the peculiar situation where a work like Musallam al-Thubut, which rivals Jam' al-Jawami' in theology, comes from Indian lands (al-Sirhindi and al-Dehlawi). He then dismisses false claims about contradictions that have no basis. Then he introduces the fourth topic: the Arab-Indian dialogue. He describes his personal efforts over many years to track down Indian treasures and build a bridge between the Arab world and India, and he has succeeded in transmitting some transmitted sciences (al-ulum al-naqliyya). However, the rational sciences (al-ulum al-aqliyya) from India remained inaccessible in Egypt, Syria, Iraq, and the Maghreb. To illustrate the difficulty, he quotes Shaykh al-Islam Hasan al-Attar, who recounts that all copies of 'Abd al-Hakim's work were corrupted until a man from Bukhara brought a correct copy, allowing al-Attar to correct an Egyptian copy. Al-Attar also mentions obtaining rare glosses by Mir Zahid al-Hindi on several works. The author praises al-Attar as an exemplary Azhari Ash'ari scholar whose efforts restored al-Azhar's prestige, contrasting with later baseless claimants. The passage concludes with two references to al-Attar's glosses. All examples in this passage are from the Islamic scholarly tradition, specifically manuscript studies and the history of transmission of Islamic sciences from India.

Key Terms
العلوم العقلية
العلوم النقلية
تحريف

The rarity and corruption of Indian rational manuscripts in the Arab world made al-Attar's correction efforts crucial for preserving these works.
