Manuscript Correction in Islamic Scholarship: al-Attar's Method
Author discusses manuscript correction and reliance on a Bukharan copy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the manuscript correction process used by al-Attar and explain its importance in preserving Islamic texts.

Core Idea
A single reliable manuscript can correct an entire tradition.

In this lesson, we examine a biographical note from al-Attar's commentary where he details how he corrected an Egyptian copy of 'Abd al-Hakim's works using a superior copy brought from Bukhara. This process reflects the rigorous scholarly standards of manuscript verification in the Islamic tradition, akin to the principles of isnad criticism in hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
Read the first part of the passage where al-Attar states that all copies of 'Abd al-Hakim are corrupted. What is the core issue he is addressing?
Corruption of manuscripts was a common problem due to scribal errors and intentional alterations.
2
Find the corrective source
Al-Attar mentions a 'very correct copy' brought by a virtuous man from Bukhara. Why is the geographical origin significant?
Bukhara was a major center of Islamic learning with a reputation for accurate transmission.
3
Understand the correction process
He 'corrected an Egyptian copy based on it' and relied on that corrected copy. What does this tell you about his method?
He used the reliable copy as an exemplar to emend the local copy, not simply replace it.
4
Assess the broader impact
Al-Attar also obtained glosses from Mir Zahid al-Hindi via a scholar from Bukhara. How does this illustrate the transnational character of Islamic scholarship?
Scholarly travel (riḥla) was essential for acquiring rare and accurate texts.

شرح بحر العلوم على سلم العلوم
العطار رحمة الله ، يقول فيه في بعض المناسبات: ... وأصل نسخ عبد الحكيم كلها محرفة .. وقد منّ الله على الفقير بنسخة من عبد الحكيم صحيحة جدا،
قدم بها رجل فاضل من ،بخاری، فصححنا عليها نسخة مصرية، وعليها اعتمدت في النقل ... ) .
ويقول في موضع آخر : ورأيت للعلامة المحقق مير زاهد الهندي تحريرا نفيسا .. ربما لا يقف عليه غيري ؛ فإن حاشيته المذكورة وكذلك حاشيته على شرح الجلال الدواني.. وحاشيته على شرح الهياكل للدواني قدم بها رجل من علماء بخارى مصر، مريدا للحج، فحصلنا منه حاشية العلامة عبد الحكيم على المواقف، وصححنا نسخة مير زاهد على الدواني.. ولم يسمح بحواشي مير زاهد ولا بغيرها من بقية الكتب التي رأيناها معه، مما لا يوجد في بلادنا، بل كنا لا نعرف أسماءها فضلا عن مسمياتها
فسبحان من أحاط بكل شيء علما ، ورحم الله شيخنا العطار، فقد ضرب أروع مثال لعالم أزهري أشعري بمثله صارت للأزهر ما كان لها من الهيبة ، وإن مزقها أصحاب الدعاوي الفارغة بعده.

لمحة موجزة عن المصنف
Sharh Bahr al-‘Ulum ‘ala Sullam al-‘Ulum. Al-‘Attar, may God have mercy on him, says in it on some occasions: ... The origin of the copies of ‘Abd al-Hakim are all corrupted. And God has favored the poor one with a copy of ‘Abd al-Hakim that is very correct, brought by a virtuous man from Bukhara, so we corrected an Egyptian copy based on it, and I relied on it in transmission. And he says in another place: I saw for the investigating scholar Mir Zahid al-Hindi a precious commentary that perhaps no one other than me has come across; for his mentioned gloss, as well as his gloss on Sharh al-Jalal al-Dawwani, and his gloss on Sharh al-Hayakil al-Dawwani, a man from the scholars of Bukhara brought them to Egypt, intending for Hajj, so we obtained from him the gloss of the scholar ‘Abd al-Hakim on al-Mawaqif, and we corrected a copy of Mir Zahid on al-Dawwani. And he did not allow [us to copy] the glosses of Mir Zahid nor others of the remaining books that we saw with him, which are not found in our lands; rather we did not even know their names, let alone their referents. So glorified is He who encompasses everything in knowledge. May God have mercy on our teacher al-‘Attar, for he set the most wonderful example of an Azhari Ash‘ari scholar, by whose like al-Azhar had the prestige it had, even if the people of empty claims tore it apart after him. Chapter Two: A Brief Glimpse of the Author.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note from the commentary Bahr al-‘Ulum, providing information about the author al-‘Attar and his work on manuscript correction. It opens with al-‘Attar's statement that the copies of ‘Abd al-Hakim are all corrupt, but God favored him with a very correct copy brought by a virtuous man from Bukhara. Using this, he corrected an Egyptian copy and relied on it for transmission. Next, al-‘Attar mentions discovering a precious commentary by Mir Zahid al-Hindi, which he obtained from a scholar from Bukhara during Hajj. He also obtained ‘Abd al-Hakim's gloss on al-Mawaqif and corrected a copy of Mir Zahid's work. The passage ends with praise for God and for al-‘Attar, describing him as an exemplary Azhari Ash‘ari scholar. The overall theme emphasizes the meticulous attention to manuscript authenticity in the Islamic scholarly tradition.

Biography of Imam Muhibbullah al-Bihari
Name, lineage, birth, and early education of Imam Muhibbullah al-Bihari

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical elements of Imam Muhibbullah al-Bihari and explain how his diverse training (fiqh, usul, philosophy, logic, kalam) shaped his contributions to Islamic logic.

Core Idea
Muhibbullah al-Bihari's mastery across multiple Islamic sciences makes his logical works uniquely authoritative.

Before diving into the logical concepts of a classical text like Sullam al-Ulum, it is essential to know the author. This biographical passage introduces us to Imam Muhibbullah al-Bihari, a towering figure in the Islamic intellectual tradition. By understanding his name, lineage, education, and the breadth of his expertise, we can better appreciate the depth and authority of his logical works.

Guided Path
1
Extract the full name and its components
Read the full name: 'Muhibbullah ibn Abd al-Shakur al-Uthmani al-Siddiqi al-Hanafi al-Bihari'. Each element carries meaning: 'al-Bihari' indicates his origin from Bihar (India), 'al-Hanafi' his school of jurisprudence, and 'al-Uthmani'/'al-Siddiqi' his lineage connections to the Caliphs Uthman and Abu Bakr. Note these affiliations.
2
List the scholarly disciplines mentioned
The passage describes him as: 'al-faqih al-usuli, al-faylasuf al-mantiqi al-mutakallim' (the jurist-usuli, philosopher-logician-theologian). Make a mental list of these fields: fiqh, usul al-fiqh, philosophy, logic, kalam. Recognise that he was not merely a logician but a polymath.
3
Identify his birthplace and early teachers
Locate the birthplace: 'Kara', a village in the Muhib Ali Fur district of Bihar. His teachers: Shaykh Mulla Qutb al-Din al-Sihalawi and 'Allama Qutb al-Din al-Husayni. Note that he studied under two prominent scholars, reading some books with the first and most with the second.
4
Connect biography to his logical works
Consider how his training in usul al-fiqh and kalam influenced his approach to logic. For example, his work 'Musallam al-Thubut' deals with the principles of jurisprudence, while 'Sullam al-Ulum' introduces logic. The integration of logical methods with other disciplines is a hallmark of his scholarship.

شخصية الإمام المحقق محب الله البهاري
الفصل الأول
شخصية الإمام المحقق محب الله البهاري
المبحث الأول : اسمه ونسبه ومولده:
هو: الشيخ الإمام محب الله بن عبد الشكور العثماني الصديقي الحنفي البِهَارِي، الفقيه الأصولي، الفيلسوف المنطقي المتكلم، أحد أجلة علماء الإسلام ومن مشاهير أذكياء العالم، ولد ونشأ في «كرا»، قرية من أعمال مُحِبٌ عَلِى فُورٌ من ولاية بِهَارُ)) ، من ولاية الهند الشمالية، وعشيرته تعرف بالملك .
المبحث الثاني: نشأته:
قرأ بعض الكتب الدَّرْسية على الشيخ المُلا قطب الدين بن عبد الحليم الأنصاري السِّهَالَوِي (٢)، وقرأ أكثرها على العلامة قطب الدين الحسيني
The personality of the verifying Imam Muhibbullah al-Bihari
Chapter One
The personality of the verifying Imam Muhibbullah al-Bihari
First Section: His name, lineage, and birth:
He is: the Shaykh Imam Muhibbullah ibn Abd al-Shakur al-Uthmani al-Siddiqi al-Hanafi al-Bihari, the jurist-usuli, the philosopher-logician-theologian, one of the great scholars of Islam and among the famous intellectuals of the world. He was born and raised in 'Kara', a village from the districts of Muhib Ali Fur in the province of Bihar, in northern India, and his clan is known as al-Malik.
Second Section: His upbringing:
He read some of the standard books under Shaykh Mulla Qutb al-Din ibn Abd al-Halim al-Ansari al-Sihalawi, and he read most of them under the scholar 'Allama Qutb al-Din al-Husayni.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage provides a biographical overview of Imam Muhibbullah al-Bihari, a prominent 18th-century Indian scholar. It opens with his full name and titles: Shaykh Imam Muhibbullah ibn Abd al-Shakur al-Uthmani al-Siddiqi al-Hanafi al-Bihari. The sequence of names indicates his lineage: 'al-Uthmani' and 'al-Siddiqi' suggest ties to the Caliphs Uthman and Abu Bakr, while 'al-Hanafi' shows his school of jurisprudence. He is described as a jurist (faqih), usuli (specialist in principles of jurisprudence), philosopher, logician, and theologian, highlighting his multidisciplinary expertise. The text states he was born and raised in 'Kara', a village in the Muhib Ali Fur district of Bihar, northern India, and his clan was known as 'al-Malik'. The second section details his education: he studied some textbooks under Shaykh Mulla Qutb al-Din al-Sihalawi, and the majority under 'Allama Qutb al-Din al-Husayni. This indicates his scholarly training under two notable teachers. The passage thus establishes the author's credentials and intellectual lineage, setting the stage for his logical works like 'Sullam al-Ulum' and 'Musallam al-Thubut'.

Biography of Muhabbullah al-Bihari: Scholarly Lineage and Context
Passage presents the biography of Muhabbullah al-Bihari, including his name, birth, teachers, and scholarly context.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical elements of Muhabbullah al-Bihari and explain the significance of his scholarly lineage for the transmission of logic and jurisprudence in the Indian subcontinent.

Core Idea
A scholar's biography is the key to understanding the authority and transmission of his works.

This passage introduces the great scholar Muhabbullah al-Bihari, the author of Bahr al-Ulum, a famous commentary on the logic text Sullam al-Ulum. Understanding his teachers, his own students, and the historical context of the Mughal Empire helps us appreciate the chain of knowledge that preserved and developed the Islamic logical tradition. This lesson will help you extract the essential biographical data and connect it to the broader intellectual history.

Guided Path
1
Extract the full name and nisba
Find all parts of his name: given name, father's name, lineage, and nisba (al-Bihari, al-Hanafi, etc.). What do these indicate about his geographical and legal school affiliation?
2
Identify his principal teachers
The passage mentions two teachers. Who are they, and what did he study under each? Note the different subjects.
3
Identify the teacher's teacher (the chain)
The passage provides details about Mulla Qutb al-Din's own teachers and background. This establishes the isnad (chain of transmission). Who are they?
4
Note the historical context
The passage mentions Sultan Aurangzeb Alamgir and the academy in Bihar. Why is this important for the development of Islamic sciences?
5
Identify the scholar's role in the transmission of logic
What is his famous work? How does this biography help authenticate his commentary on al-Sullam?

شخصية الإمام المحقق محب الله البهاري
الفصل الأول
شخصية الإمام المحقق محب الله البهاري
المبحث الأول : اسمه ونسبه ومولده:
هو: الشيخ الإمام محب الله بن عبد الشكور العثماني الصديقي الحنفي البِهَارِي، الفقيه الأصولي، الفيلسوف المنطقي المتكلم، أحد أجلة علماء الإسلام ومن مشاهير أذكياء العالم، ولد ونشأ في «كرا»، قرية من أعمال مُحِبٌ عَلِى فُورٌ من ولاية بِهَارُ)) ، من ولاية الهند الشمالية، وعشيرته تعرف بالملك.
المبحث الثاني: نشأته:
قرأ بعض الكتب الدَّرْسية على الشيخ المُلا قطب الدين بن عبد الحليم الأنصاري السِّهَالَوِي (٢)، وقرأ أكثرها على العلامة قطب الدين الحسيني الشمس آبادي، ثم رحل إلى معسكر السلطان عالمكير ، وكان من بلاد قصبة من أعمال الكهنو»، أصله من شيوخ «سهالي»، وشيوخها فريقان: أنصاريون من نسل الأنصار الله ، وعثمانيون من نسل سيدنا عثمان رضي اللَّه عَنهُ ، ورئاسة «سهالي» متعلقة رَضِوَاللَّهُ بكليهما، والملا قطب الدين من الشيوخ الأنصاريين.
أخذ العلوم عن الملا دانيال الجوراسي - نسبة إلى جوراس بفتح الجيم وسكون الواو والراء والألف والسين المهملة - قصبة من قصبات الفورب، وهو تلميذ الملا عبد السلام الديوي - نسبة إلى ديوه، بكسر الدال المهملة وسكون التحتانية وفتح الواو والهاء في الآخر أيضا قصبة من قصبات الفورب - وأخذ الطريقة الجشتية عن القاضي كاسي بن داود الإله آبادي، وهو تلميذ الشيخ محب الله الإله آبادي صاحب رسالة التسوية في التصوف وشارح «الفصوص» بالفارسية، وأكمل خلفائه .
والملا قطب الدين كان صائم الدهر، قائم الليل، يختم القرآن في التهجد كل ليلة، إمام الأساتذة ومقدام الجهابذة، معدن العقليات ومخزن النقليات، صرف عمره في شغل التدريس، وانتهت إليه رئاسة العلم في «الفورب»، وله على شرح العقائد العضدية للعلامة الدواني حاشية في غاية الدقة، وحاشية على الأمور العامة، وعلى التلويح، وعلى شرح حكمة العين، تلفت أكثرها ليلة قُتِلَ على يد الظالمين ، إثر نزاع جرى بين طائفتين، وكان ذلك سنة ثلاث ومائة وألف (۱۱۰۳هـ ) ، وله إذ ذاك ثلاث وستون سنة. أبنائه ومن العلامة الشيخ نظام الدين السهالوي والد بحر العلوم، شارح السلم، كما سنعرف ذلك بعد قليل. انظر سبحة المرجان في آثار هندستان لغلام علی بلكرامي: ٧٦، وانظر أيضا نزهة الخواطر لعبد الحي الحسني اللكهنوي: ٧٨٤، ٠٧٨٥ (۱) هو : الإمام المجاهد المظفر المنصور السلطان أبو المظفر، محيي الدين محمد أوْرَنْكَزيب عَالَمْكِيرْ بن شاهجهان ، أعظم ملوك الهند ديانة وصيانة، صاحب الفتوحات العظيمة، ولد ليلة الأحد لخمس عشرة خلون من ذي القعدة عام ۱۰۲۸هـ ، بقرية «دوحد»، قرأ العلم على مولانا عبد اللطيف السلطانفوري ومولانا محمد هاشم الكيلاني والشيخ محيني بن عبد الله البهاري وغيرهم وبايع الشيخ محمد معصوم بن الشيخ أحمد السرهندي، جلس على سرير الملك عام ١٠٦٨هـ ، كان حنفي المذهب سنيا ماتريدي المعتقد، صنف الدين أربعين حديثا، وبأمره صنف علماء الهند (الفتاوى العالمكيرية الفتاوى الهندية
The personality of the verifying Imam Muhabbullah al-Bihari. Chapter One: The personality of the verifying Imam Muhabbullah al-Bihari. First research: His name, lineage, and birth. He is: the Shaykh, the Imam, Muhabbullah son of Abd al-Shakur al-Uthmani al-Siddiqi al-Hanafi al-Bihari, the jurist, the usuli, the philosopher, the logician, the theologian, one of the great scholars of Islam and among the famous geniuses of the world. He was born and raised in 'Kara', a village from the district of Muhabbat Ali Fur in the province of Bihar, in the province of northern India, and his clan is known as al-Malik. Second research: His upbringing. He read some of the academic books under the Shaykh, the Mulla Qutb al-Din ibn Abd al-Halim al-Ansari al-Sihalawi (2), and he read most of them under the scholar Qutb al-Din al-Husayni al-Shams Abadi. Then he travelled to the camp of Sultan Alamgir, and he was from a town, a small town from the districts of al-Kahanu? His origin was from the shaykhs of 'Sihali', and its shaykhs are two groups: Ansaris from the descendants of the Ansar (may Allah be pleased with them), and Uthmanis from the descendants of our master Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him), and the leadership of 'Sihali' belongs to both of them. And Mulla Qutb al-Din is from the Ansari shaykhs. He acquired knowledge from Mulla Daniyal al-Jurasi - attributed to Jurasi with fatha on jim, sukun on waw and ra and alif and sin mu'jamah - a small town from the towns of al-Fur? He is the student of Mulla Abd al-Salam al-Diyawi - attributed to Diyuh, with kasr on dal muhmalah, sukun on ta' and under it, and fatha on waw and ha in the end, also a small town from al-Fur? - and he took the Chishti order from Qadi Kasi ibn Dawood al-Ilahabadi, who is the student of Shaykh Muhabbullah al-Ilahabadi, the author of Risalat al-Taswiyah in tasawwuf and the commentator on 'al-Fusus' in Persian, and the most complete of his successors. And Mulla Qutb al-Din was a perpetual faster, a night-stayer, he would complete the Quran in the night prayer every night, the imam of teachers and the pioneer of geniuses, the mine of rational sciences and the storehouse of transmitted sciences. He spent his life in the occupation of teaching, and the leadership of knowledge in 'al-Fur' ended with him. He has a gloss on Sharh al-Aqa'id al-Adudiyyah by al-Dawwani that is extremely precise, and a gloss on al-Umur al-'Ammah, and on al-Talwih, and on Sharh Hikmat al-'Ayn. Most of them were lost on the night he was killed by oppressors, after a conflict occurred between two groups, and that was in the year 1103 AH, and he was then 63 years old. Among his sons is the scholar Shaykh Nizam al-Din al-Sihalawi, the father of Bahr al-Ulum, the commentator on al-Sullam, as we will know that shortly. See Subhat al-Marjan fi Athar al-Hindistan by Ghulam Ali al-Balgrami: 76, and also see Nuzhat al-Khawatir by Abd al-Hayy al-Hasani al-Laknawi: 784, 0785. (1) He is: the mujahid, the victorious, the helped Imam, Sultan Abu al-Muzaffar, Muhyi al-Din Muhammad Aurangzeb Alamgir ibn Shahjahan, the greatest of the kings of India in piety and chastity, possessor of great conquests, born on the night of Sunday, fifteen nights remaining of Dhu al-Qa'dah in the year 1028 AH, in the village of 'Duhad'. He read knowledge under our master Abd al-Latif al-Sultanfuri, and our master Muhammad Hashim al-Kilani, and Shaykh Muhyini ibn Abd Allah al-Bahari and others, and he pledged allegiance to Shaykh Muhammad Ma'sum ibn Shaykh Ahmad al-Sarhindi. He sat on the throne of kingship in the year 1068 AH. He was Hanafi in madhhab, Sunni, Maturidi in doctrine. He authored a book of forty hadiths, and by his order the scholars of India authored (al-Fatawa al-Alamgiriyya, al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya).
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of the scholar Muhabbullah al-Bihari, known as Bahr al-Ulum, the author of the commentary on Sullam al-Ulum (a famous text on logic). The passage begins by introducing his full name, lineage, and birthplace: he is Muhabbullah ibn Abd al-Shakur al-Bihari, a Hanafi jurist, usuli, philosopher, logician, and theologian, born and raised in the region of Bihar in northern India. It then describes his studies under two teachers: first, Mulla Qutb al-Din al-Sihalawi, from whom he read some books, and second, the scholar Qutb al-Din al-Husayni, from whom he read most of his texts. The passage also details the background of his teacher Qutb al-Din al-Sihalawi, including his own teachers, his spiritual lineage in the Chishti order, his scholarly achievements, and his tragic death in 1103 AH at the hands of oppressors following a conflict. The biography mentions Qutb al-Din's character as a perpetual faster and night-prayer reciter, and his expertise in both rational and transmitted sciences, as well as his glosses on several important works. It also notes that one of Qutb al-Din's sons was Nizam al-Din al-Sihalawi, the father of Bahr al-Ulum (i.e., our author). Additionally, the passage provides a brief biography of Sultan Aurangzeb Alamgir, under whose patronage many scholars worked, and mentions the compilation of the Fatawa Alamgiriyya. This passage serves to establish the scholarly credentials and context of Muhabbullah al-Bihari, whose commentary on Sullam al-Ulum is the subject of the present work.

Tracing a Scholar's Lineage and Tribal Affiliation
Biography of Mulla Qutb al-Din, his lineage, teachers, character, and death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two main scholarly families in Sahali and explain Mulla Qutb al-Din's place within them.

Core Idea
Tribal lineage shapes a scholar's identity and scholarly network.

Understanding a scholar's tribal background is crucial for situating him within the broader Islamic intellectual tradition. This passage introduces the two tribal groups of Sahali: Ansaris and Uthmanis, and places Mulla Qutb al-Din among the Ansaris. This lesson will teach you how to extract such lineage information from a biographical text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the town and its groups
Read the passage to find the name of the town (Sahali) and the two groups of shaykhs that govern it. The text says: 'وشيوخها فريقان: أنصاريون من نسل الأنصار ... وعثمانيون من نسل سيدنا عثمان'.
Note that both groups are linked to noble lineages: the Ansar (helpers of the Prophet) and Uthman (the third caliph).
2
Determine Mulla Qutb al-Din's affiliation
The passage explicitly states: 'والملا قطب الدين من الشيوخ الأنصاريين'. This tells you he belongs to the Ansari branch.
This affiliation may have implications for his scholarly authority in the region.
3
Understand the significance of dual leadership
The text says 'ورئاسة سهالي متعلقة بكليهما' meaning leadership belongs to both groups. This reflects a leadership structure shared between Ansaris and Uthmanis.
Such equilibrium is interesting for understanding social organization in Indian Muslim communities.

Commentary of Bahr al-Ulum on Sullam al-Ulum. Shams Abadi, then he traveled to the camp of Sultan Alamgir, and he was from a town, a district from the works of al-Kahnu? His origin is from the shaykhs of Sahali, and its shaykhs are two groups: Ansaris from the descendants of the Ansar, may Allah be pleased with them, and Uthmanis from the descendants of our master Uthman, may Allah be pleased with him, and the leadership of Sahali belongs to both of them, and Mulla Qutb al-Din is from the Ansari shaykhs. He took knowledge from Mulla Daniel al-Jurasi – attribution to Juras, with fatha on jim, sukun on waw and ra, alif and sin muhmala – a district from the districts of Furp, and he is the student of Mulla Abd al-Salam al-Diwi – attribution to Diwa, with kasra on dal muhmala, sukun on tahtaniyya, fatha on waw and ha at the end, also a district from the districts of Furp – and he took the Chishtiyya path from Qadi Kasi ibn Dawud al-Ilahabadi, and he is the student of Shaykh Muhabbah Allah al-Ilahabadi, author of the epistle al-Taswiya in Sufism and commentator on al-Fusus in Persian, and the most complete of his successors. And Mulla Qutb al-Din was one who fasted perpetually, stood in night prayer, completed the Quran in tahajjud every night, the imam of teachers and the spearhead of geniuses, the mine of rational sciences and the storehouse of transmitted sciences, he spent his life in the occupation of teaching, and the leadership of knowledge in Furp ended with him. He has a gloss on the commentary on al-Aqa'id al-Adudiyya by al-Allama al-Dawani of utmost precision, and a gloss on al-Umur al-Amma, and on al-Talwih, and on the commentary on Hikmat al-Ayn, most of which were lost on the night he was killed by the oppressors, following a conflict that occurred between two sects, and that was in the year 1103 AH, and he was then sixty-three years old. Among his sons is al-Allama Shaykh Nizam al-Din al-Sahalawi, the father of Bahr al-Ulum, the commentator on al-Sullam, as we will know that shortly. See Subhat al-Marjan fi Athar Hindistan by Ghulam Ali Balkrami: 76, and also see Nuzhat al-Khawatir by Abd al-Hayy al-Hasani al-Lakhnawi: 784, 785. (1) He is: the Imam, the mujahid, the victorious, the helped, Sultan Abu al-Muzaffar, Muhy al-Din Muhammad Awrangzib Alamgir ibn Shahjahan, the greatest of the kings of India in religion and piety, possessor of great conquests, born on the night of Sunday, fifteen nights remaining from Dhu al-Qa'da in the year 1028 AH, in the village of Duhad. He studied knowledge under Mawlana Abd al-Latif al-Sultanfuri and Mawlana Muhammad Hashim al-Kilani and Shaykh Muhini ibn Abd Allah al-Bahari and others, and gave allegiance to Shaykh Muhammad Ma'sum ibn Shaykh Ahmad al-Sirhindi. He sat on the throne of kingship in the year 1068 AH. He was of the Hanafi school, Sunni, Maturidi in creed. He authored forty hadiths, and by his order the scholars of India compiled al-Fatawa al-Alamgiriyya al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of Mulla Qutb al-Din al-Sahalawi, a prominent Indian scholar. It begins by noting his lineage from the Ansari shaykhs of the town of Sahali. It then details his education: he studied under Mulla Daniel al-Jurasi and Mulla Abd al-Salam al-Diwi, and took the Chishtiyya Sufi path from Qadi Kasi ibn Dawud al-Ilahabadi, who was a student of Shaykh Muhabbah Allah al-Ilahabadi. Next, it describes Mulla Qutb al-Din's personal piety—he was perpetually fasting, prayed night vigil, and completed the Quran nightly—and his scholarly stature, being a leading teacher and authority in Furp. The passage lists his glosses on several works, which were mostly lost when he was killed in a sectarian conflict in 1103 AH at age 63. Finally, it mentions that among his sons was Shaykh Nizam al-Din al-Sahalawi, the father of the author of Bahr Ulum (the commentary on Sullam al-Ulum), and provides references for further reading. A footnote on Sultan Alamgir is included, describing his lineage, birth, education, reign, and his role in compiling the Fatawa Alamgiriyya.

Mapping the Chain of Transmission (Sanad)
Biography of Mulla Qutb al-Din, his lineage, teachers, character, and death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a teacher-student chain from the passage and identify the Sufi lineage.

Core Idea
A scholar's chain of teachers forms his intellectual and spiritual genealogy.

The passage provides a clear chain of teachers for Mulla Qutb al-Din, both in formal Islamic sciences and in the Chishtiyya Sufi path. This lesson will teach you to extract and reconstruct such chains, which are foundational in hadith sciences and Sufi initiations.

Guided Path
1
List the teachers of Mulla Qutb al-Din in the Islamic sciences
The text mentions 'الملا دانيال الجوراسي' and 'الملا عبد السلام الديوي'. Note that Abd al-Salam al-Diwi is the teacher of Daniel al-Jurasi.
These teachers are linked to the region of Furp.
2
Identify the Sufi chain (silsila)
Mulla Qutb al-Din took the Chishtiyya path from 'القاضي كاسي بن داود الإله آبادي', who was a student of 'الشيخ محب الله الإله آبادي'.
The Sufi chain often goes through multiple shaykhs back to the founder.
3
Reconstruct the complete chain
Combine the information: Mulla Qutb al-Din ← Qadi Kasi ← Shaykh Muhabbah Allah for the Chishtiyya chain; and for sciences: Mulla Qutb al-Din ← Mulla Daniel ← Mulla Abd al-Salam.
This method mirrors isnad analysis in hadith.

والملا قطب الدين كان صائم الدهر، قائم الليل، يختم القرآن في التهجد كل ليلة، إمام الأساتذة ومقدام الجهابذة، معدن العقليات ومخزن النقليات، صرف عمره في شغل التدريس، وانتهت إليه رئاسة العلم في «الفورب»، وله على شرح العقائد العضدية للعلامة الدواني حاشية في غاية الدقة، وحاشية على الأمور العامة، وعلى التلويح، وعلى شرح حكمة العين، تلفت أكثرها ليلة قُتِلَ على يد الظالمين ، إثر نزاع جرى بين طائفتين، وكان ذلك سنة ثلاث ومائة وألف (۱۱۰۳هـ ) ، وله إذ ذاك ثلاث وستون سنة. أبنائه ومن العلامة الشيخ نظام الدين السهالوي والد بحر العلوم، شارح السلم، كما سنعرف ذلك بعد قليل. انظر سبحة المرجان في آثار هندستان لغلام علی بلكرامي: ٧٦، وانظر أيضا نزهة الخواطر لعبد الحي الحسني اللكهنوي: ٧٨٤، ٠٧٨٥ (۱) هو : الإمام المجاهد المظفر المنصور السلطان أبو المظفر، محيي الدين محمد أوْرَنْكَزيب عَالَمْكِيرْ بن شاهجهان ، أعظم ملوك الهند ديانة وصيانة، صاحب الفتوحات العظيمة، ولد ليلة الأحد لخمس عشرة خلون من ذي القعدة عام ۱۰۲۸هـ ، بقرية «دوحد»، قرأ العلم على مولانا عبد اللطيف السلطانفوري ومولانا محمد هاشم الكيلاني والشيخ محيني بن عبد الله البهاري وغيرهم وبايع الشيخ محمد معصوم بن الشيخ أحمد السرهندي، جلس على سرير الملك عام ١٠٦٨هـ ، كان حنفي المذهب سنيا ماتريدي المعتقد، صنف
الدين
أربعين حديثا، وبأمره صنف علماء الهند (الفتاوى العالمكيرية الفتاوى الهندية
Commentary of Bahr al-Ulum on Sullam al-Ulum. Shams Abadi, then he traveled to the camp of Sultan Alamgir, and he was from a town, a district from the works of al-Kahnu? His origin is from the shaykhs of Sahali, and its shaykhs are two groups: Ansaris from the descendants of the Ansar, may Allah be pleased with them, and Uthmanis from the descendants of our master Uthman, may Allah be pleased with him, and the leadership of Sahali belongs to both of them, and Mulla Qutb al-Din is from the Ansari shaykhs. He took knowledge from Mulla Daniel al-Jurasi – attribution to Juras, with fatha on jim, sukun on waw and ra, alif and sin muhmala – a district from the districts of Furp, and he is the student of Mulla Abd al-Salam al-Diwi – attribution to Diwa, with kasra on dal muhmala, sukun on tahtaniyya, fatha on waw and ha at the end, also a district from the districts of Furp – and he took the Chishtiyya path from Qadi Kasi ibn Dawud al-Ilahabadi, and he is the student of Shaykh Muhabbah Allah al-Ilahabadi, author of the epistle al-Taswiya in Sufism and commentator on al-Fusus in Persian, and the most complete of his successors. And Mulla Qutb al-Din was one who fasted perpetually, stood in night prayer, completed the Quran in tahajjud every night, the imam of teachers and the spearhead of geniuses, the mine of rational sciences and the storehouse of transmitted sciences, he spent his life in the occupation of teaching, and the leadership of knowledge in Furp ended with him. He has a gloss on the commentary on al-Aqa'id al-Adudiyya by al-Allama al-Dawani of utmost precision, and a gloss on al-Umur al-Amma, and on al-Talwih, and on the commentary on Hikmat al-Ayn, most of which were lost on the night he was killed by the oppressors, following a conflict that occurred between two sects, and that was in the year 1103 AH, and he was then sixty-three years old. Among his sons is al-Allama Shaykh Nizam al-Din al-Sahalawi, the father of Bahr al-Ulum, the commentator on al-Sullam, as we will know that shortly. See Subhat al-Marjan fi Athar Hindistan by Ghulam Ali Balkrami: 76, and also see Nuzhat al-Khawatir by Abd al-Hayy al-Hasani al-Lakhnawi: 784, 785. (1) He is: the Imam, the mujahid, the victorious, the helped, Sultan Abu al-Muzaffar, Muhy al-Din Muhammad Awrangzib Alamgir ibn Shahjahan, the greatest of the kings of India in religion and piety, possessor of great conquests, born on the night of Sunday, fifteen nights remaining from Dhu al-Qa'da in the year 1028 AH, in the village of Duhad. He studied knowledge under Mawlana Abd al-Latif al-Sultanfuri and Mawlana Muhammad Hashim al-Kilani and Shaykh Muhini ibn Abd Allah al-Bahari and others, and gave allegiance to Shaykh Muhammad Ma'sum ibn Shaykh Ahmad al-Sirhindi. He sat on the throne of kingship in the year 1068 AH. He was of the Hanafi school, Sunni, Maturidi in creed. He authored forty hadiths, and by his order the scholars of India compiled al-Fatawa al-Alamgiriyya al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of Mulla Qutb al-Din al-Sahalawi, a prominent Indian scholar. It begins by noting his lineage from the Ansari shaykhs of the town of Sahali. It then details his education: he studied under Mulla Daniel al-Jurasi and Mulla Abd al-Salam al-Diwi, and took the Chishtiyya Sufi path from Qadi Kasi ibn Dawud al-Ilahabadi, who was a student of Shaykh Muhabbah Allah al-Ilahabadi. Next, it describes Mulla Qutb al-Din's personal piety—he was perpetually fasting, prayed night vigil, and completed the Quran nightly—and his scholarly stature, being a leading teacher and authority in Furp. The passage lists his glosses on several works, which were mostly lost when he was killed in a sectarian conflict in 1103 AH at age 63. Finally, it mentions that among his sons was Shaykh Nizam al-Din al-Sahalawi, the father of the author of Bahr Ulum (the commentary on Sullam al-Ulum), and provides references for further reading. A footnote on Sultan Alamgir is included, describing his lineage, birth, education, reign, and his role in compiling the Fatawa Alamgiriyya.

Key Terms
الجشتية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
From whom did Mulla Qutb al-Din take the Chishtiyya path?
A) Mulla Daniel al-Jurasi
B) Mulla Abd al-Salam al-Diwi
C) Qadi Kasi ibn Dawud al-Ilahabadi
D) Shaykh Muhabbah Allah al-Ilahabadi

Key Takeaway
Mulla Qutb al-Din's teachers form a chain linking him to earlier scholars, both in Islamic sciences and in the Chishtiyya Sufi order.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

From the passage, write out the Chishtiyya chain from Mulla Qutb al-Din back to Shaykh Muhabbah Allah, noting each link.

Assessing a Scholar's Piety and Scholarly Output
Biography of Mulla Qutb al-Din, his lineage, teachers, character, and death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify characteristics of a traditional scholar's piety and list his major works from the biography.

Core Idea
A scholar's piety and scholarly output are essential for evaluating his legacy.

The passage paints a vivid picture of Mulla Qutb al-Din's devout lifestyle and his impressive list of glosses. This lesson will teach you to extract such biographical details and understand their significance in the Islamic scholarly tradition.

Guided Path
1
Find descriptions of piety
Scan the Arabic for phrases like 'صائم الدهر، قائم الليل، يختم القرآن في التهجد كل ليلة'. These indicate perpetual fasting, night prayer, and completing the Quran nightly.
Such descriptions are common in biographical entries to highlight a scholar's devotion.
2
List his authored works
The text mentions four glosses (حاشية) on: 1) شرح العقائد العضدية لدواني, 2) الأمور العامة, 3) التلويح, 4) شرح حكمة العين. Note that most were lost.
These works show his expertise in kalam, philosophy, and usul.
3
Assess his teaching career
The text says 'صرف عمره في شغل التدريس، وانتهت إليه رئاسة العلم في الفورب', indicating he spent his life teaching and became the leading authority in Furp.
Teaching and leading are key marks of a scholar's influence.

Understanding the Political and Sectarian Context of a Scholar's Death
Biography of Mulla Qutb al-Din, his lineage, teachers, character, and death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the circumstances of Mulla Qutb al-Din's death and its impact on his legacy.

Core Idea
A scholar's death often reflects the volatile political and sectarian environment of his time.

Mulla Qutb al-Din was killed in a sectarian conflict at age 63. This lesson will help you extract the details of his death from the passage and understand how such events affect the preservation of a scholar's works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the year and cause of death
The text says 'سنة ثلاث ومائة وألف (1103هـ)' and 'قتل على يد الظالمين إثر نزاع جرى بين طائفتين'.
The cause is sectarian conflict, and the perpetrators are called 'oppressors'.
2
Note the loss of his works
Most of his glosses were lost on the night of his murder: 'تلفت أكثرها ليلة قتل'.
This loss is a tragedy for Islamic scholarship.
3
Reflect on the broader context
The footnote about Sultan Alamgir (a contemporary) indicates the political landscape of Mughal India, where sectarian tensions existed.
Understanding this context is key to evaluating the safety of scholars.

He took knowledge from Mulla Daniel al-Jurasi – attribution to Juras, with fatha on jim, sukun on waw and ra, alif and sin muhmala – a district from the districts of Furp, and he is the student of Mulla Abd al-Salam al-Diwi – attribution to Diwa, with kasra on dal muhmala, sukun on tahtaniyya, fatha on waw and ha at the end, also a district from the districts of Furp – and he took the Chishtiyya path from Qadi Kasi ibn Dawud al-Ilahabadi, and he is the student of Shaykh Muhabbah Allah al-Ilahabadi, author of the epistle al-Taswiya in Sufism and commentator on al-Fusus in Persian, and the most complete of his successors. He has a gloss on the commentary on al-Aqa'id al-Adudiyya by al-Allama al-Dawani of utmost precision, and a gloss on al-Umur al-Amma, and on al-Talwih, and on the commentary on Hikmat al-Ayn, most of which were lost on the night he was killed by the oppressors, following a conflict that occurred between two sects, and that was in the year 1103 AH, and he was then sixty-three years old. Among his sons is al-Allama Shaykh Nizam al-Din al-Sahalawi, the father of Bahr al-Ulum, the commentator on al-Sullam, as we will know that shortly. See Subhat al-Marjan fi Athar Hindistan by Ghulam Ali Balkrami: 76, and also see Nuzhat al-Khawatir by Abd al-Hayy al-Hasani al-Lakhnawi: 784, 785. (1) He is: the Imam, the mujahid, the victorious, the helped, Sultan Abu al-Muzaffar, Muhy al-Din Muhammad Awrangzib Alamgir ibn Shahjahan, the greatest of the kings of India in religion and piety, possessor of great conquests, born on the night of Sunday, fifteen nights remaining from Dhu al-Qa'da in the year 1028 AH, in the village of Duhad. He studied knowledge under Mawlana Abd al-Latif al-Sultanfuri and Mawlana Muhammad Hashim al-Kilani and Shaykh Muhini ibn Abd Allah al-Bahari and others, and gave allegiance to Shaykh Muhammad Ma'sum ibn Shaykh Ahmad al-Sirhindi. He sat on the throne of kingship in the year 1068 AH. He was of the Hanafi school, Sunni, Maturidi in creed. He authored forty hadiths, and by his order the scholars of India compiled al-Fatawa al-Alamgiriyya al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of Mulla Qutb al-Din al-Sahalawi, a prominent Indian scholar. It begins by noting his lineage from the Ansari shaykhs of the town of Sahali. It then details his education: he studied under Mulla Daniel al-Jurasi and Mulla Abd al-Salam al-Diwi, and took the Chishtiyya Sufi path from Qadi Kasi ibn Dawud al-Ilahabadi, who was a student of Shaykh Muhabbah Allah al-Ilahabadi. Next, it describes Mulla Qutb al-Din's personal piety—he was perpetually fasting, prayed night vigil, and completed the Quran nightly—and his scholarly stature, being a leading teacher and authority in Furp. The passage lists his glosses on several works, which were mostly lost when he was killed in a sectarian conflict in 1103 AH at age 63. Finally, it mentions that among his sons was Shaykh Nizam al-Din al-Sahalawi, the father of the author of Bahr Ulum (the commentary on Sullam al-Ulum), and provides references for further reading. A footnote on Sultan Alamgir is included, describing his lineage, birth, education, reign, and his role in compiling the Fatawa Alamgiriyya.

Connecting a Scholar to a Famous Commentary (Bahr Ulum)
Biography of Mulla Qutb al-Din, his lineage, teachers, character, and death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the relationship between Mulla Qutb al-Din and the commentary Bahr Ulum on Sullam al-Ulum.

Core Idea
Mulla Qutb al-Din is the grandfather of the commentator Bahr al-Ulum.

The passage concludes by mentioning that among Mulla Qutb al-Din's sons is Shaykh Nizam al-Din, who is the father of Bahr al-Ulum (the commentator of Sullam al-Ulum). This lesson will help you trace the scholarly lineage within a family and understand the interconnectedness of Islamic scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key familial relationship
The text says: 'ومن أبنائه العلامة الشيخ نظام الدين السهالوي والد بحر العلوم، شارح السلم'. So Mulla Qutb al-Din is the father of Shaykh Nizam al-Din, who is the father of Bahr al-Ulum.
Thus, Mulla Qutb al-Din is the grandfather of the commentator.
2
Understand the significance
Bahr al-Ulum wrote the commentary on Sullam al-Ulum, which is the subject of this course. Knowing his grandfather provides continuity in the scholarly tradition.
This shows that knowledge often runs in families.
3
Verify with cross-references
The passage gives citations: Subhat al-Marjan and Nuzhat al-Khawatir for further reading.
These references confirm the relationship.

The Life and Career of Imam Muhy al-Din al-Bahari
Biographical overview of al-Bahari's career and appointments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key events in al-Bahari's career and explain how his positions contributed to his scholarly output.

Core Idea
Al-Bahari's life as a judge, teacher, and advisor shaped his mastery of logic and law.

Imam Muhy al-Din al-Bahari was not only a logician but also a qadi and tutor to royalty. Understanding his biography helps us appreciate the context of his logical works, which were written amid political shifts. In this lesson, we trace his career from Lucknow to Hyderabad to Kabul.

Guided Path
1
Locate the timeline
Find the years mentioned: his move to Lucknow, transfer to Hyderabad, then to Kabul with Rafi' al-Qadr, and finally his appointment as Sadr by Shah Alam in 1118 AH. Mark these points.
2
Identify his titles
He was appointed qadi (judge) in Lucknow and Hyderabad, then became a teacher (mu'allim) for Rafi' al-Qadr, and later was given the title Fadil Khan when he became Sadr al-Sudur. Note the progression.
His title 'Fadil Khan' indicates his scholarly status.
3
Connect his positions to his works
His judicial and teaching roles required deep knowledge of logic and usul al-fiqh. His works Sullam al-Ulum and al-Ifadat were likely written during these periods.
The fact that he authored foundational logic texts while serving as a judge shows the integration of rational sciences in Islamic judiciary.

Personality of the verifying Imam Muhabbah Allah al-Bahari. In the Deccan, he appointed him to the judgeship of the city of Lucknow, then after a period he transferred him to Hyderabad, then he dismissed him from the judgeship and made him a teacher for Rafi' al-Qadr ibn Shah Alam ibn Alamgir. And when Shah Alam ruled over the lands of Kabul and traveled there, he took him along with his son Rafi' al-Qadr, so he resided there for a time. Then when Shah Alam assumed kingship after his father Alamgir in the year 1118 AH, he appointed him to the great presidency (sadr) and titled him Fadil Khan in the year 1119 AH / 1707 CE. The third section: His works. Al-Allama al-Bahari is considered among the most prominent contributors in the field of authorship and composition in the Islamic sciences, possessing abundant fortune and great share in this art. He has eternal scholarly works in the rational and transmitted sciences, indicating his scholarly personality and imamate in the religion. Hence some of his biographers said: 'Sufficient for you as a witness to the abundance of his knowledge is al-Sullam and al-Muslim.' Below is a brief presentation of his works, may Allah have mercy on him. (1). 1. Sullam al-Ulum fi Ilm al-Mantiq, which is a unique book, not woven after its pattern, and it precedes Musallam al-Thubut, as we will indicate. Its discussion will come in its own chapter in the following section. 2. al-Ifadat fi Ilm al-Mantiq, and this book I have not found anyone mentioning in the list of his works, and the author referred to it in the beginning of the first article of al-Muslim, where he said: 'Among them – i.e., the principles – are logical, because they made it part of kalam, and we have completed it in al-Sullam and al-Ifadat' (2). = (1) In six large volumes, and he spent one hundred thousand coins on their compilation. And he died in Deccan in the year 1118 AH. See a good portion of his biography in Nuzhat al-Khawatir: 737-743, and Mu'jam al-Matbu'at al-Arabiyya by Sarkis: 1/595. (2) Musallam al-Thubut: 17/1.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage provides a biographical sketch of Imam Muhy al-Din al-Bahari and a list of his major works. It begins by recounting his career: he served as judge in Lucknow and Hyderabad, then as teacher to Rafi' al-Qadr, and eventually was appointed to the grand sadr (religious head) by Shah Alam with the title Fadil Khan. Then the third section (of the book) presents his works. It states that al-Bahari is a prominent author in Islamic sciences, and that his works Sullam al-Ulum and Musallam al-Thubut testify to his knowledge. The first work listed is Sullam al-Ulum fi Ilm al-Mantiq, described as unique and precedent over Musallam al-Thubut. The second is al-Ifadat fi Ilm al-Mantiq, which is less well-known; the author references it in his own work al-Muslim. Footnotes provide additional details on the compilation of al-Fatawa al-Alamgiriyya and references for al-Bahari's biography.

Al-Bahari's Major Works on Logic: Sullam al-Ulum and al-Ifadat
Overview of al-Bahari's works, especially Sullam al-Ulum and al-Ifadat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between al-Bahari's two major logic works – Sullam al-Ulum and al-Ifadat – and state the relationship between Sullam al-Ulum and Musallam al-Thubut.

Core Idea
Sullam al-Ulum is a unique and precedent logic manual; al-Ifadat is a lesser-known work referenced within it.

Al-Bahari authored two known works on logic: Sullam al-Ulum, which is highly celebrated, and al-Ifadat, which is less known and rarely mentioned. The passage also claims that Sullam al-Ulum precedes Musallam al-Thubut. In this lesson, we examine the descriptions of these works.

Guided Path
1
Extract the titles and descriptions
The passage lists two works: 'سلم العلوم' and 'الإفادات'. Note their descriptions: Sullam is 'فريد، لم ينسج على منواله' (unique, not patterned after another) and precedes Musallam al-Thubut. Al-Ifadat is referred to in al-Muslim.
2
Understand the claim of precedence
The author says Sullam al-Ulum is متقدم على مسلم الثبوت (precedes Musallam al-Thubut). This could mean chronologically or in methodological priority. Note that Musallam al-Thubut is a later work, possibly on usul al-fiqh.
Sullam al-Ulum is often used as a primer for logic before tackling more advanced works.
3
Find the reference to al-Ifadat
The passage includes a quotation from al-Muslim: 'فمنها المنطقية ... وقد فرغنا عنها في السلم والإفادات' (we have completed them in al-Sullam and al-Ifadat). This shows that al-Ifadat is another one of al-Bahari's logic texts.
The fact that al-Bahari mentions al-Ifadat in al-Muslim indicates it was written earlier.

Personality of the verifying Imam Muhabbah Allah al-Bahari. In the Deccan, he appointed him to the judgeship of the city of Lucknow, then after a period he transferred him to Hyderabad, then he dismissed him from the judgeship and made him a teacher for Rafi' al-Qadr ibn Shah Alam ibn Alamgir. And when Shah Alam ruled over the lands of Kabul and traveled there, he took him along with his son Rafi' al-Qadr, so he resided there for a time. Then when Shah Alam assumed kingship after his father Alamgir in the year 1118 AH, he appointed him to the great presidency (sadr) and titled him Fadil Khan in the year 1119 AH / 1707 CE. The third section: His works. Al-Allama al-Bahari is considered among the most prominent contributors in the field of authorship and composition in the Islamic sciences, possessing abundant fortune and great share in this art. He has eternal scholarly works in the rational and transmitted sciences, indicating his scholarly personality and imamate in the religion. Hence some of his biographers said: 'Sufficient for you as a witness to the abundance of his knowledge is al-Sullam and al-Muslim.' Below is a brief presentation of his works, may Allah have mercy on him. (1). 1. Sullam al-Ulum fi Ilm al-Mantiq, which is a unique book, not woven after its pattern, and it precedes Musallam al-Thubut, as we will indicate. Its discussion will come in its own chapter in the following section. 2. al-Ifadat fi Ilm al-Mantiq, and this book I have not found anyone mentioning in the list of his works, and the author referred to it in the beginning of the first article of al-Muslim, where he said: 'Among them – i.e., the principles – are logical, because they made it part of kalam, and we have completed it in al-Sullam and al-Ifadat' (2). = (1) In six large volumes, and he spent one hundred thousand coins on their compilation. And he died in Deccan in the year 1118 AH. See a good portion of his biography in Nuzhat al-Khawatir: 737-743, and Mu'jam al-Matbu'at al-Arabiyya by Sarkis: 1/595. (2) Musallam al-Thubut: 17/1.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage provides a biographical sketch of Imam Muhy al-Din al-Bahari and a list of his major works. It begins by recounting his career: he served as judge in Lucknow and Hyderabad, then as teacher to Rafi' al-Qadr, and eventually was appointed to the grand sadr (religious head) by Shah Alam with the title Fadil Khan. Then the third section (of the book) presents his works. It states that al-Bahari is a prominent author in Islamic sciences, and that his works Sullam al-Ulum and Musallam al-Thubut testify to his knowledge. The first work listed is Sullam al-Ulum fi Ilm al-Mantiq, described as unique and precedent over Musallam al-Thubut. The second is al-Ifadat fi Ilm al-Mantiq, which is less well-known; the author references it in his own work al-Muslim. Footnotes provide additional details on the compilation of al-Fatawa al-Alamgiriyya and references for al-Bahari's biography.

Key Terms
سلم العلوم
الإفادات
مسلم الثبوت

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway

Biography of Imam Muhabib Allah al-Bihari
Author narrates the life and appointments of al-Bihari.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the career progression of Imam al-Bihari and identify the key political offices he held.

Core Idea
A scholar's biography reveals the contexts shaping his intellectual authority.

Al-Bihari's life is not just a list of dates; it shows how his scholarly career intertwined with Mughal politics. From judge in Lucknow to supreme chancellor, his appointments reflect the trust of the imperial family. This lesson helps you map his career and understand the significance of the titles he earned.

Guided Path
1
Locate the geographical arc
Note the cities mentioned: Deccan (origin), Lucknow, Hyderabad, Kabul. This shows his movements across the Mughal empire.
2
Sequence the appointments
List the positions in order: judge (qadi) in Lucknow → transferred to Hyderabad → removed from judgeship → tutor to Rafi' al-Qadr → supreme chancellor (al-sadarat al-uzma).
Notice the progression from a local religious post to a high imperial office.
3
Identify the key terms
Focus on 'al-sadarat al-uzma' (supreme chancellorship) and the title 'Fadil Khan'. These are markers of his status.
The title 'Fadil Khan' means 'virtuous lord', a honorific granted by the emperor.
4
Contextualize with dates
The year 1119 AH (1707 CE) marks his appointment as chancellor after Shah Alam's accession. Relate this to historical events like the death of Aurangzeb (Alamgir) in 1707.

شخصية الإمام المحقق محب الله البهاري . «الدكن، فولاه القضاء بمدينة «لكهنو»، ثم نقله بعد مدة إلى «حيدر آباد» ، ثم عزله عن القضاء وجعله معلما لرفيع القدر بن شاه عالم بن عالمكير، ولما ولي شاه عالم على بلاد (کابل) وسافر إليها استصحبه مع ولده رفيع القدر، فأقام بها ،زمانا ثم لما قام شاه عالم بالملك بعد والده عالمكير سنة ١١١٨هـ ، ولاه الصدارة العظمى، ولقبه فاضل خان سنة ١١١٩هـ /١٧٠٧م.
The personality of the verifying Imam Muhabib Allah al-Bihari. He hailed from Deccan, and he was appointed as judge in the city of Lucknow, then he was transferred after a while to Hyderabad, then he was removed from the judiciary and made a teacher for Rafi' al-Qadr, son of Shah Alam son of Alamgir. When Shah Alam took charge of the land of Kabul and traveled there, he took him along with his son Rafi' al-Qadr, so he stayed there for a time. Then when Shah Alam assumed kingship after his father Alamgir in the year 1118 AH, he appointed him to the supreme chancellorship and titled him Fadil Khan in the year 1119 AH / 1707 CE.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch of Imam Muhabib Allah al-Bihari. It opens by identifying him as a 'verifying imam', then recounts his career: first as a judge in Lucknow, then transferred to Hyderabad, then dismissed from judgeship and appointed as tutor to Rafi' al-Qadr, a prince. When Shah Alam became king, al-Bihari was appointed to the highest administrative position ('al-sadarat al-uzma') and given the title Fadil Khan. The narrative follows the chronological order of his appointments, illustrating his close connection to the Mughal ruling family. The mention of specific years and locations grounds his biography in historical context.

Introduction to Musallam al-Thubut and Its Author
Biographical introduction to Musallam al-Thubut and its author

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical and historical facts about Musallam al-Thubut and its author, Muhibullah al-Bihari, and explain the book's significance in Usul al-Fiqh.

Core Idea
Musallam al-Thubut became a foundational text in Usul al-Fiqh through its wide circulation and scholarly endorsements.

This lesson introduces you to the celebrated Usul al-Fiqh text Musallam al-Thubut and its author, Muhibullah al-Bihari. Understanding a book's origin and reception helps you assess its authority in the Islamic scholarly tradition. We will explore how its title encodes its date via the abjad system, trace its print history, and appreciate why it attracted commentaries and was printed alongside al-Ghazali's al-Mustasfa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book and author
Locate the phrase 'Musallam al-Thubut' and note that it is a work on Usul al-Fiqh by Muhibullah al-Bihari, written in 1109 AH. The passage emphasises that all sources attribute it to him.
The author's full name is often given as Muhibullah al-Bihari; he flourished in the 12th century AH.
2
Understand the title's abjad derivation
The title 'Musallam al-Thubut' is calculated using the abjad system, indicating its composition year (1109 AH). The author himself stated this in the introduction.
Abjad assigns numerical values to letters, so the title's letters sum to 1109.
3
Note the print history and its significance
The passage lists several Indian editions (Aligarh, Delhi) and mentions a Bulaq press edition printed together with al-Ghazali's al-Mustasfa. This shows the book's wide acceptance and demand.
Multiple printings in different regions indicate scholarly interest and continuous use.
4
Recognise praise and commentaries
The passage quotes al-Attar's praise at the end of his gloss on Jam' al-Jawami', and notes that many prominent scholars wrote commentaries on Musallam al-Thubut.
Commentaries (shuruh) are a key indicator of a text's importance in the madrasa curriculum.
5
Apply to evaluate the book's status
Consider why the Bulaq press chose to print it with al-Mustasfa: it suggests Musallam al-Thubut was considered at least as valuable as al-Ghazali's classic.
This comparison helps you gauge the book's rank in the Usul al-Fiqh tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من شرح بحر العلوم على سلم العلوم
مسلم الثبوت في علم أصول الفقه ألفه عام ١١٠٩هـ، كما يؤخذ اسمه «مسلم الثبوت» طبقا لحساب الجمل، وقد صرح بذلك في مقدمته. ومسلم الثبوت نسبته إليه في جميع المصادر التي تتحدث عن العلامة البهاري. وقد طبع مرات في الهند ومصر وبيروت فمن طبعاته الهندية: طبعة عليكره الهند عام ١٢٩٧هـ /۱۸۷۹م، طبع الحجر، وطبعة المطبعة المجتبائية بـ «دهلي» الهند، عام ١٣١١هـ /۱۸۹۳م، وطبع بعناية المولوي محمد عبد اللطيف والمولوي محمد عبد الحكيم بـ«دهلي» الهند، عام ١٣١٧هـ /١٨٩٩م، هذا بالإضافة إلى طبعاته الهندية الأخرى لشروح هذا الكتاب، كما سنعرف ذلك فيما يلي. وهو وحده كاف للدلالة على عبقريته الابتكارية وعظمته العلمية؛ حيث تفرد بمميزات كثيرة، ليس هنا محل بسطها، ورأينا فيما سبق كيف أن العلامة العطار يثني على هذا الكتاب في أواخر حاشيته على شرح جمع الجوامع. فلا غرابة في اختيار مطبعة بولاق العتيقة بمصر المحمية مع كتاب المستصفى للغزالي لتطبعهما معا في كتاب واحد يُكوّن مجلدين، وطبع في عام ١٣٢٥هـ. وتصدى لشرح هذا الكتاب طائفة من العلماء البارزين.
From the commentary Bahr al-Ulum on Sullam al-Ulum. Musallam al-Thubut in the science of Usul al-Fiqh, authored in the year 1109 AH, as its name 'Musallam al-Thubut' is taken according to the calculation of the abjad system, and he declared that in his introduction. And Musallam al-Thubut is attributed to him in all sources that speak about the scholar al-Bihari. It has been printed many times in India, Egypt, and Beirut. Among its Indian editions: the Aligarh edition of 1297 AH / 1879 CE, lithograph; the edition of the Mujtaba'iyya press in Delhi, India, in 1311 AH / 1893 CE; and the edition under the supervision of Mawlana Muhammad Abd al-Latif and Mawlana Muhammad Abd al-Hakim in Delhi, India, in 1317 AH / 1899 CE. This is in addition to other Indian editions of commentaries on this book, as we will know later. It alone is sufficient to indicate his innovative genius and scientific greatness, as it is distinguished by many characteristics, which are not the place to elaborate here. We saw earlier how the scholar al-Attar praised this book in the end of his gloss on the commentary on Jam' al-Jawami'. So it is no surprise that the ancient Bulaq press in protected Egypt chose it together with al-Ghazali's al-Mustasfa to print them together in one book forming two volumes, printed in 1325 AH. And a group of prominent scholars undertook to write commentaries on this book.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to the work Musallam al-Thubut and its author, Muhibullah al-Bihari. It first identifies the book as a text on Usul al-Fiqh composed in 1109 AH, noting that its title is derived from the abjad numerical value. The author then confirms that the book is universally attributed to al-Bihari in all sources. The passage details various Indian printings, including lithographs from Aligarh and Delhi, showing the book's wide circulation. It then praises the book as evidence of the author's innovative genius, mentioning that al-Attar praised it at the end of his gloss on Sharh Jam' al-Jawami'. The passage highlights that the Bulaq press printed it alongside al-Ghazali's al-Mustasfa in a single two-volume set in 1325 AH, indicating its high regard. Finally, it notes that many prominent scholars wrote commentaries on Musallam al-Thubut, leading into the subsequent enumeration.

Key Takeaway
Musallam al-Thubut's abjad title, multiple printings, and the fact that it was printed alongside al-Ghazali's al-Mustasfa demonstrate its foundational status in Usul al-Fiqh.

Seven Commentators on Musallam al-Thubut
Enumerates seven prominent scholars who wrote commentaries on Musallam al-Thubut.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the seven commentators on Musallam al-Thubut and their respective works as listed in the passage.

Core Idea
Musallam al-Thubut attracted commentaries from seven major scholars spanning India.

This passage enumerates seven prominent scholars who wrote commentaries on the usul al-fiqh text Musallam al-Thubut. Knowing these names and their works helps you trace the scholarly tradition and see how this text was transmitted and taught.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and first commentator
The passage begins by naming Muhibullah al-Bihari as the author. The first commentator listed is Bahr al-Ulum Abd Ali, whose commentary on al-Sullam is the focus of the present work. Note that his biography will follow later.
2
Survey the commentators and their works
Read through items 2 to 7. For each, note the commentator's full name, the title of his commentary, and any publication details (e.g., al-Qanuji's Kashf al-Mubham printed in Kanpur).
3
Recognize geographical and temporal spread
Most commentators are from India, with dates ranging roughly from the 13th to 14th centuries AH. This indicates the text's importance in the Indian subcontinent and the scholarly network around it.

شخصية الإمام المحقق محب الله البهاري
١ - بحر العلوم عبد العلي، صاحب شرح السلم الذي انتدبنا له الآن، وستأتي ترجمته.
٢ - بشير الدين القاضي بن كريم الدين العثماني القنوجي (١٢٣٤ - ١٢٩٦هـ)، شرحه في كتاب اسمه كشف المبهم فيما في المسلم، طبع في كانفور عام ١٢٨٧هـ / ۱۸۷۰م، وفي عام ١٣٠٧هـ /١٨٩٠ ۹۱م، طبع الحجر.

٥ - العلامة الشيخ عبد الحق بن فضل حق الخيرآبادي، له شرح على مسلم الثبوت، وقد طبع هذا الشرح بالمطبعة النظامية في «كانفور» الهند، بدون تاريخ.

The personality of the verifying imam Muhibullah al-Bihari. 1 - Bahr al-Ulum Abd Ali, author of the commentary on al-Sullam which we are now engaged with, and his biography will come. 2 - Bashir al-Din al-Qadi bin Karim al-Din al-Uthmani al-Qanuji (1234-1296 AH), his commentary in a book called Kashf al-Mubham fima fi al-Muslim, printed in Kanpur in 1287 AH / 1870 CE, and in 1307 AH / 1890-91 CE, lithograph. 3 - The scholar Mawlana Wali bin Habib Allah al-Lakhnawi, he has Nafa'is al-Malakut fi Sharh Musallam al-Thubut. 4 - Mawla Hasan bin Ghulam Mustafa al-Lakhnawi, he has a commentary on Musallam al-Thubut. 5 - The scholar Shaykh Abd al-Haqq bin Fadl Haqq al-Khayrabadi, he has a commentary on Musallam al-Thubut, and this commentary was printed at the Nizamiyya press in Kanpur, India, without date. 6 - Shaykh Ahmad Abd al-Haqq al-Lakhnawi, he has a commentary on Musallam al-Thubut. 7 - Shaykh Muhammad Sharif al-Mustafabadi al-Hindi, he has al-Taqrir al-Aslam.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage provides a numbered list of seven commentators on Musallam al-Thubut. It begins by naming the author, Muhibullah al-Bihari, as the subject of the biography. The first commentator listed is Bahr al-Ulum Abd Ali, the author of the commentary on al-Sullam that is the focus of the present work, with a note that his biography will follow. The second is Bashir al-Din al-Qadi al-Qanuji, whose work Kashf al-Mubham was printed in Kanpur in 1287 and 1307 AH. The third is Wali bin Habib Allah al-Lakhnawi, author of Nafa'is al-Malakut. The fourth is Hasan bin Ghulam Mustafa al-Lakhnawi, who wrote a commentary. The fifth is Abd al-Haqq al-Khayrabadi, whose commentary was printed at the Nizamiyya press without date. The sixth is Ahmad Abd al-Haqq al-Lakhnawi, also a commentator. The seventh is Muhammad Sharif al-Mustafabadi, author of al-Taqrir al-Aslam. This enumeration shows the significant scholarly attention this work received.

Biographical Overview of Commentators on Muslim al-Thubut
Lists scholars who wrote commentaries on Muslim al-Thubut and related works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify key commentators on Muslim al-Thubut and trace the chain of commentary that transmitted this work through the Indian scholarly tradition.

Core Idea
The commentary tradition on Muslim al-Thubut shows how a foundational logic text was transmitted and enriched within the Indian subcontinent.

In the Islamic intellectual tradition, a text's authority is often measured by its commentary tradition. Muslim al-Thubut, a core work in logic and usul al-fiqh, attracted numerous commentators, especially in India. This lesson introduces you to the scholars who engaged with this text, helping you understand how knowledge was passed down and expanded.

Guided Path
1
Identify the foundational text
Locate the name Muslim al-Thubut and note its significance as a work on logic and usul al-fiqh. Recognize that it is the base text for multiple commentaries.
The text is by Muhibb Allah al-Bahari.
2
List the commentators
Go through the passage and list each commentator mentioned, along with their commentary title. Pay attention to names and their honorifics.
The first seven are: Bahr al-Ulum, Bashir al-Din al-Qanuji, Wali ibn Habib Allah, Hasan ibn Ghulam Mustafa, Abd al-Haqq al-Khayrabadi, Ahmad Abd al-Haqq, Muhammad Sharif al-Mustafabadi.

In Islamic education, knowing the commentators validates the text's study.

Commentary
This passage provides a biographical and bibliographical list of scholars who commented on the work Muslim al-Thubut and related texts. The author begins by noting the personality of Imam Muhibb Allah al-Bahari, then enumerates seven commentators and their works: 1) Bahr al-Ulum Abd al-Ali (author of the commentary on Sullam al-Ulum); 2) Bashir al-Din al-Qanuji, who wrote Kashf al-Mubham; 3) Wali ibn Habib Allah al-Lakhnawi, author of Nafais al-Malakut; 4) Hasan ibn Ghulam Mustafa al-Lakhnawi; 5) Abd al-Haqq al-Khayrabadi; 6) Ahmad Abd al-Haqq al-Lakhnawi; 7) Muhammad Sharif al-Mustafabadi. The author also mentions that Bahr al-Ulum wrote a Persian translation of Muslim al-Thubut. The passage then notes that despite Indian scholarly interest, the book did not spread widely outside India. Additional glosses and treatises are listed, including a gloss on Sullam al-Ulum, a gloss on Muslim al-Thubut (unfound), a book al-Jawhar al-Fard, and a treatise on fallacies with a commentary by Muhammad Abd al-Halim. This is purely biographical and bibliographical, with no logical arguments.

Al-Bahari's Life and Works: Context for Sullam al-Ulum
Author lists al-Bahari's works and extols his scholarly stature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major works of Imam Muhibb Allah al-Bahari and explain how his biography informs the study of his logical poem Sullam al-Ulum.

Core Idea
Al-Bahari's stature as a logician and usuli justifies why Sullam al-Ulum is a core text in Muslim logic.

Every great text has a great author. Before diving into the logical intricacies of Sullam al-Ulum, it is essential to appreciate the scholarly weight of its author, Imam Muhibb Allah al-Bahari. This lesson situates al-Bahari within the Islamic intellectual tradition and lists his key writings, showing why his works—especially Sullam al-Ulum—deserve careful study.

Guided Path
1
List al-Bahari's major works
From the passage, extract the names of all works attributed to al-Bahari. Note especially Sullam al-Ulum (logic) and Muslim al-Thubut (usul al-fiqh).
The passage also mentions treatises on atomism and fallacies.
2
Assess his geographical influence
The author states that al-Bahari's works were of interest in India but did not spread outside as they should. Consider what this implies about the circulation of knowledge.
This limitation may affect how widely his ideas are studied today.
3
Identify testimonies of his rank
Find the explicit statements about al-Bahari's scholarly stature, including the comparison to Abd al-Hakim al-Siyalkuti. Why does the author mention this?
Such testimonies establish the credibility of the text.
4
Connect biography to the commentary
The passage is from a modern commentary on Sullam al-Ulum. How does knowing about al-Bahari's life and works prepare you to study his logic?
Understanding the author's background helps you appreciate the depth of his logical system.

This passage is a biographical introduction by the author of the modern scholarly work (Bahr Ulum) about Imam Muhibb Allah al-Bahari, the 17th-century Indian logician and usuli. The passage first lists the works of al-Bahari, including Sullam al-Ulum, Muslim al-Thubut, and treatises on atomism and fallacies. It then extols his scholarly rank, mentioning that contemporaries like Sheikh Hasan al-Attar compared him to Abd al-Hakim al-Siyalkuti. The author emphasizes that al-Bahari's two principal works in logic and usul al-fiqh are sufficient to demonstrate his elevated standing. The passage sets the stage for studying al-Bahari's Sullam al-Ulum, the commentary on which is the subject of this book.

Evaluating Scholarly Authority: Testimony, Works, and Depth
Methodology for establishing scholarly status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three criteria used in this passage to establish a scholar's standing and apply them to a given scholar.

Core Idea
A scholar's rank is known through the testimony of peers, the quality of his major works, and the depth of his ideas.

This passage from the introduction to a commentary on al-Bihari's logic text presents a concise methodology for recognizing scholarly excellence. The author mentions three distinct indicators: the acknowledgments of those who have studied his legacy, a direct comparison to a renowned master by a reputable shaykh, and the evidence provided by his two major works. Understanding this methodology helps us navigate the Islamic tradition's way of establishing authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three indicators
List them as mentioned in the passage: (a) acknowledgment of those who examined his legacy, (b) specific testimony of Shaykh Hasan al-‘Attar comparing him to al-Siyalkuti, (c) the evidence of his two books.
2
Analyze the function of testimonies
Consider why the author quotes another scholar's opinion rather than just stating his own. This reflects the Islamic academic practice of relying on qualified witnesses.
3
Evaluate the role of major works
The passage says merely looking at the two books confirms the testimonies. Why are books considered sufficient evidence? Because they represent the scholar's mature thought.
4
Appreciate the author's methodological restraint
The author chooses not to engage in a deep analysis because it would take too long and the book itself will demonstrate the author's rank. What does this tell us about the purpose of the introduction?

المبحث الرابع: شخصيته العلمية: اعترف كل من اطلع على تراث هذا الإمام بعلو منزلته وجلالة قدره، وتبحره في العلوم، وسبق أن نقلنا كلام الشيخ حسن العطار فيه، ووصفه بأنه في درجة عبد الحكيم السيالكوتي. وبمجرد الاطلاع على كتابيه: «مسلم الثبوت في الأصول وسلم العلوم في المنطق يتبين لنا صدق شهادات هؤلاء. ثم إذا تعمقنا في دراسة تراثه وقمنا بتحليل آرائه وأفكاره نجد صدارته وإمامته حقيقة واضحة ملموسة، إلا أن ذلك يأخذ وقتا طويلا، ويحتاج إلى أطول، فلا أصرف الوقت في ذلك، ونحن أمام كتابه «السلم»، وسوف يقوم بواجبه إن شاء الله تعالى.
Fourth Section: His Scientific Personality: Everyone who has examined the legacy of this Imam has acknowledged his lofty rank, great status, and profound knowledge in the sciences. We have previously transmitted the words of Shaykh Hasan al-‘Attar about him, describing him as being at the level of ‘Abd al-Hakim al-Siyalkuti. Merely by looking at his two books, ‘Muslim al-Thubut in al-Usul’ and ‘Sullam al-‘Ulum in Logic’, we realize the truth of these testimonies. Then if we deeply study his legacy and analyze his opinions and ideas, we find his leadership and imamate to be a clear and tangible reality, except that this takes a long time and requires more time, so I will not spend time on that, and we are in front of his book ‘al-Sullam’, and it will fulfill its duty, God willing.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note from the editor or commentator about the author, Muhabbatullah al-Bihari. It begins by stating that everyone who has studied his works recognizes his high rank. It then quotes Shaykh Hasan al-‘Attar comparing him to ‘Abd al-Hakim al-Siyalkuti, a major figure in the later tradition. The passage emphasizes that just looking at his two major works—‘Muslim al-Thubut’ in usul al-fiqh and ‘Sullam al-‘Ulum’ in logic—confirms these praises. It then says a deep study would take too long, so the focus will be on the book at hand, ‘al-Sullam’.

Al-Bihari's Two Major Works and Their Significance
Introduction to al-Bihari's two masterworks

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two works mentioned and explain why they are considered proof of al-Bihari's scholarly rank.

Core Idea
Muslim al-Thubut and Sullam al-‘Ulum are the twin pillars of al-Bihari's reputation in usul al-fiqh and logic.

In this passage, the author points to al-Bihari's two books as immediate evidence of his profound knowledge. One is a foundational text in usul al-fiqh, the other a widely used manual in logic. Recognizing these works and their fields helps us understand the breadth of al-Bihari's expertise.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two books
Find the names in the Arabic: 'مسلم الثبوت في الأصول' and 'سلم العلوم في المنطق'.
2
Determine their fields
The first is in usul al-fiqh (principles of jurisprudence), the second in mantiq (logic).
3
Understand why they are evidence
The passage says merely looking at them confirms the testimonies. What does it mean for a book to be a 'proof'? It means the quality and depth of the work speak for themselves.
4
Reflect on the author's focus
The author of the commentary is focusing on the logic text (al-Sullam). How does this relate to the author's purpose?

Fourth Section: His Scientific Personality: Everyone who has examined the legacy of this Imam has acknowledged his lofty rank, great status, and profound knowledge in the sciences. We have previously transmitted the words of Shaykh Hasan al-‘Attar about him, describing him as being at the level of ‘Abd al-Hakim al-Siyalkuti. Merely by looking at his two books, ‘Muslim al-Thubut in al-Usul’ and ‘Sullam al-‘Ulum in Logic’, we realize the truth of these testimonies. Then if we deeply study his legacy and analyze his opinions and ideas, we find his leadership and imamate to be a clear and tangible reality, except that this takes a long time and requires more time, so I will not spend time on that, and we are in front of his book ‘al-Sullam’, and it will fulfill its duty, God willing.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note from the editor or commentator about the author, Muhabbatullah al-Bihari. It begins by stating that everyone who has studied his works recognizes his high rank. It then quotes Shaykh Hasan al-‘Attar comparing him to ‘Abd al-Hakim al-Siyalkuti, a major figure in the later tradition. The passage emphasizes that just looking at his two major works—‘Muslim al-Thubut’ in usul al-fiqh and ‘Sullam al-‘Ulum’ in logic—confirms these praises. It then says a deep study would take too long, so the focus will be on the book at hand, ‘al-Sullam’.
