Biographical details and scholarly praise of Bahr Ulum
Concludes biography with death date and praise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract key biographical details from a traditional scholar's death notice and evaluate the significance of scholarly praise in Islamic biographical literature.

Core Idea
A scholar's death notice encapsulates his legacy and the esteem of his peers.

This passage marks the conclusion of a biography, providing the precise date and place of Bahr Ulum's death, his burial site, and a powerful tribute from a later historian. Understanding how to read such notices is essential for anyone studying the lives of Islamic scholars and the intellectual networks that connect them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the date and place of death
Locate the exact date (month, day, year in Hijri and Gregorian) and the city. The text states 12th Rajab 1225 AH in Madras. Note the precision: this is typical for scholarly biographies.
2
Find the burial information
The text mentions burial in the courtyard of al-Wala Jahi mosque the next day. This indicates the community's respect and provides a physical location for his grave.
3
Extract the author's prayer for the deceased
The author prays, 'May God have mercy on him with the mercy of the righteous, and grant him a garden beneath which rivers flow.' This is a standard du'a that shows the author's personal reverence.
4
Analyze the scholarly praise quoted
The author quotes Sayyid Abd al-Hayy al-Hasani from Nuzhat al-Khawatir, calling Bahr Ulum 'one of the wonders of the time and the beauties of India.' Identify the source and the hyperbolic language used to elevate the subject.
Nuzhat al-Khawatir is a major biographical dictionary of Indian scholars; quoting it adds authority.
5
Connect the praise to the broader tradition
Such praise serves to memorialize the scholar and establish his authority. In Islamic history, biographical notices (tarajim) are primary sources for evaluating a scholar's reliability and impact.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث الخامس: وفاته وثناء العلماء عليه: وكانت وفاته رَحِمَهُ اللهُ لاثنتي عشرة من شهر رجب، سنة خمس وعشرين ومائتين وألف (١٢٢٥هـ / ۱۸١٠م) ، بـ (مدراس) ، ودفن في اليوم التالي بفناء المسجد الولاجاهي) ، فرحمه الله رحمة الأبرار، وأسكنه جنة تجري تحتها الأنهار وجملة القول فيه ما قاله السيد عبد الحي الحسني في نزهة الخواطر: إنه كان من عجائب الزمن ومحاسن الهند يرجع إليه أهل كل فن في فنهم
The fifth topic: His death and the praise of scholars upon him: His death, may God have mercy on him, occurred on the twelfth of the month of Rajab, in the year one thousand two hundred and twenty-five (1225 AH / 1810 CE), in Madras, and he was buried the following day in the courtyard of the Wala Jahi mosque. May God have mercy on him with the mercy of the righteous, and grant him a garden beneath which rivers flow. The sum of the statement about him is what Sayyid Abd al-Hayy al-Hasani said in Nuzhat al-Khawatir: He was one of the wonders of the time and the beauties of India; the people of every art refer to him in their art.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note providing details of the death of the author, Bahr Ulum, and includes praise from later scholars. It states that he died on the 12th of Rajab, 1225 AH, in Madras (Chennai), and was buried at the Wala Jahi mosque. The author prays for mercy for him. The passage then quotes Sayyid Abd al-Hayy al-Hasani's praise from his work Nuzhat al-Khawatir, describing Bahr Ulum as a wonder of his time and one of the beauties of India, to whom scholars of all disciplines turned for guidance. This reflects the high esteem in which Bahr Ulum was held.

Key Terms
الولاجاهي
نزهة الخواطر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Biographical death notices in Islamic literature provide precise details that anchor a scholar's legacy and often include laudatory quotations that affirm his authority across disciplines.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
